# Age of Storms 

# Tale of bygone years

There was darkness before  
And there will be darkness after

The tales have been told since mortals have first gathered around the fire. Tales of the strange and wondrous things hidden in the vast unknown shadows of the world. Tales of creatures divine and beasts demonic; of gods and kings; of myths and monsters; from dark forests to the lands of ice; from desert wastes to the storm thrashed seas. Every corner of Deluvia has its stories to tell. Legends of h

Heroes and the villains they encounter; of the wilderness and the dangers within. Stories of battles of love of order and chaos.   
War and disease; religious and social upheaval;  the untameable ferocity of the natural world; and the monsters lurking in the deep.

\[The inhabitants of Deluvia will look to the heroic players to  heal their sorrows, and ease their regrets. The players are thrown into a broken world already operating in the aftermath of destruction, easing the regrets of the characters as they awaken to fulfill their destiny.\]

Believing the key to their future lies among the Outlands, many have ventured out to discover them. All have failed, but hope has arrived with some newcomers

Rites of passage for story progression

# Ancient History

**\[NARRATIVE POETRY\]**

      *Neath the sea, the land sinketh	the stars[^1] dimmeth,*  
                       *Gusheth forth steam	and gutting fire,*  
                       *To the very heavens	soar the hurtling flames*  
*The old wyrm swallows the moons	in mighty rage*  
               *In the threatening waters	thou finds the endless  sleep*  
	  
			**From The Deluvicon Poettica**

## The Age of Dragons \-*12,000 januul \- 0 januul*

This is the epoch of high magic.  This is as far back as any chronicler can imagine. This age, is in fact, forgotten by men. It is told that the first dragon was born of an primordial egg floating in the aether sea. She hatched and her name was Bubuntu, and from her breath the fire combined with the water and land was formed and the steam formed the cloud sea. From her breath her children were born. The dragons ruled for eons. The dragons created magic that they tapped from and wielded upon all of Deluvia. All history of this period is lost except that current mages know how to cast magic that Deluvia is imbued with. Very few sages and mystics can speak of this history.

**Bubuntu** \- the Mother of all dragons. She bore all the dragons. Her children then ate her absorbing all the aspects of Deluvia between themselves.

**Moshrog** \- The first dragon on the Aether fog sea. The dragon of void and chaos  
**Nihlheeg** \- The dragon of death. She bites at the roots of the tree of life.  
**Gogifroz** \- the dragon of cold and of the waters of the deep and the springs that come from the deep. Her breath freezes all. Swims among the cloud sea  
**Seendhyn** \- The dragon of poison. Contaminates with her breath  
**Muspelflam** \- The dragon of fire, lava. Boils in the deep  
**Nolhaug** \- The dragon of dirt and soil burrows through all the solid layers of Deluvia  
**Serpenbath** \- The dragon of the 2 Stars of day Serbroth and Penbroth, he flies carrying the balls of fire which warms and lights Deluvia  
 (btw the Star of Night, is actually a rock moon, but referred to as a star, is called Dargunbroth)  
**Turg** \- the dragon of nature and life whose offsprings blood nurtures living things  
**Arond** \- the dragon of wind and air whose breath circles and moves around Deluvia  
**Gyrzong** \- the dragon of lightning and storms. Whose fighting amongst his brothers crashes and energizes the skies   
**Mynmeen** \-  the dragon of the moons and of night, who swallows the moons during the day and spits them out again at night. Dargunbroth (breath of less dark)  is the Night Star, the moon that presides over the moons. It is called a star, because it was mistakenly described as such during early astrologication. The servant moons as they are called, are name Gharmynith (old moon) and Felmmynith (young moon)  
**Progurt** \- the dragon of stone. Chews on the stone and creates new ores from his breath. 

Each dragon breathed their elements from the void into existence to form the world known as Deluvia. From these elements the structure and power of Deluvia herself was made. The dragons existed for eons and their breath made the elements.   
From the combination of their breath were also made the gods.

Moshrog (chaos) \+ Nihlheeg (death) \= **Necromensus \<\<**  
Moshrog (chaos) \+ Gogifroz (water) \=  **Kelvora**  
Moshrog (chaos) \+ Seendhyn (water) \= **Astorius \<\<**  
Moshrog (chaos) \+ Muspelflam (fire) \= **Hythlodaeus**  
Moshrog (chaos) \+ Nolhaug (dirt) \= **Alpea**  
Moshrog (chaos) \+ Serpenbath (stars) \= **Reyus**  
Moshrog (chaos) \+ Turg (life) \= **Tresola \<\<**  
Moshrog (chaos) \+ Arond (air) \= **Aethera \<\<**  
Moshrog (chaos) \+ Gyrzong (storms) \= **Omgion**  **\<\<**  
Moshrog (chaos) \+ Mynmeen (moon) \= **Milupi \<\<**  
Moshrog (chaos) \+ Progurt (stone) \= **Rogi**

Nihlheeg (death) \+ Gogifroz (water) \= **Freg**  
Nihlheeg (death) \+ Seendhyn (water) \= **Ethys  \<\<**  
Nihlheeg (death) \+ Muspelflam (fire) \= **Baphomaticus \<\<**  
Nihlheeg (death) \+ Nolhaug (dirt) \= **Haug**  
Nihlheeg (death) \+ Serpenbath (stars) \= **Rebulus**  
Nihlheeg (death) \+ Turg (life) \= **Zweihanar  \<\<**  
Nihlheeg (death) \+ Arond (air) \= **Anona**  
Nihlheeg (death) \+ Gyrzong (storms) \= **Wark**  
Nihlheeg (death) \+ Mynmeen (moon) \= **Incubol**  
Nihlheeg (death) \+ Progurt (stone) \= **Hedus**

Gogifroz (cold) \+ Seendhyn (poison) \= **Rig**  
Gogifroz (cold) \+ Muspelflam (fire) \= **Leyacant**  
Gogifroz (cold) \+ Nolhaug (dirt) \= **Bref**  
Gogifroz (cold) \+ Serpenbath (stars) \= **Urdorz**  
Gogifroz (cold) \+ Turg (life) \=  **Boralherrog**  
Gogifroz (cold) \+ Arond (air) \= **Volsong**  
Gogifroz (cold) \+ Gyrzong (storms) \= **Iztax**  
Gogifroz (cold) \+ Mynmeen (moon) \= **Boralumugheil  \<\<**  
Gogifroz (cold) \+ Progurt (stone) \= **Boralrig**

Seendhyn (poison) \+ Muspelflam (fire) \= **Volystet  \<\<**  
Seendhyn (poison) \+ Nolhaug (dirt) \= **Noxhortes**  
Seendhyn (poison) \+ Serpenbath (stars) \= **Dragiyu  \<\<**  
Seendhyn (poison) \+ Turg (life) \= **Mirapot**  
Seendhyn (poison) \+ Arond (air) \= **Mephinox**  
Seendhyn (poison) \+ Gyrzong (storms) \= **Corrdia**  
Seendhyn (poison) \+ Mynmeen (moon) \= **Heesta**  
Seendhyn (poison) \+ Progurt (stone) \= **Milsti**

Muspelflam (fire) \+ Nolhaug (dirt) \= **Embreas \<\<**  
Muspelflam (fire) \+ Serpenbath (stars) \= **Forgi**  
Muspelflam (fire) \+ Turg (life) \= **Siltiho**  
Muspelflam (fire) \+ Arond (air) \= **Bellit**  
Muspelflam (fire) \+ Gyrzong (storms) \= **Aneath**  
Muspelflam (fire) \+ Mynmeen (moon) \= **Boirlos**  
Muspelflam (fire) \+ Progurt (stone) \= **Anvos**

Nolhaug (dirt) \+ Serpenbath (stars) \= **Viko**  
Nolhaug (dirt) \+ Turg (life) \= **Heegmos  \<\<**  
Nolhaug (dirt) \+ Arond (air) \= **Talluk**  
Nolhaug (dirt) \+ Gyrzong (storms) \= **Anagol**  
Nolhaug (dirt) \+ Mynmeen (moon) \= **Seethdor**  
Nolhaug (dirt) \+ Progurt (stone) \= **Managulus**

Serpenbath  (stars) \+ Turg (life) \= **Sifaneus \<\<**  
Serpenbath  (stars) \+ Arond (air) \= **Pallas \<\<**  
Serpenbath  (stars) \+ Gyrzong (storms) \= **Snogrok**  
Serpenbath  (stars) \+ Mynmeen (moon) \= **Heen**  
Serpenbath  (stars) \+ Progurt (stone) \= **Brimlok**

Turg (life) \+ Arond (air) \= **Finora \<\<**  
Turg (life) \+ Gyrzong (storms) \= **Hepritu**  
Turg (life) \+ Mynmeen (moon) \= **Meena**  
Turg (life) \+ Progurt (stone) \= **Zeer**

Arond (air) \+ Gyrzong (storms) \= **Corporia**  
Arond (air) \+ Mynmeen (moon) \= **Repistal**  
Arond (air) \+ Progurt (stone) \=  **Arrygheil**

Gyrzong (cold) \+ Mynmeen (moon) \= **Deptris**  
Gyrzong (cold) \+ Progurt (stone) \= **Wokfrid**

Mynmeen (moon) \+   Progurt(stone) \=  **Brogghil**

For a thousand generations the gods reigned. They created, destroyed, and quarreled

*The gods that make it through to the Age of Man have the  \<\< after them.*  
For the others have been forgotten by men and it is the worst thing for a god to be forgotten. Some fringe cults may worship the forgotten gods, but these gods have less power. For their power comes from mortals remembering them, and worshipping them

From the combination steam of the fires and ice of the breath of dragons came the gods. They are considered children of the dragons for they were born of their breath. This is The Second Age, or the Age of the Gods. the gods were many and each had their own domain. The trickster god, **Milupi** tricked the dragons into a million year hibernation. The gods created many domains of land, sky and sea and created beings called Mortals and ruled over Deluvia for a million years.  The gods had their own power bestowed in them which they waged war upon each other. The gods were jealous of magic of Mortals because it was a power they didn’t have, and a power that came from the elements deep in Deluvia, from the dragons; and the gods suppressed magic for the million years.

Here is the genealogy of the gods.  
In the Age of Gods, **Boralumugheil**, cast the land in darkness, frost and hibernation to keep his daughter, **Embreas** from being courted by **Necromensus,** (this is the metaphor of fire and ice) for they were at war with each other. Necromensus and Embreas were still secretly wed and their daughter **Freymiss** was born to grow and bring the end of the hibernation by killing her grandfather, Boralumugheil. As he lay in her arms, from her grief and guilt she shed a tear that became frozen and as it fell to the frozen ground, broke into three shards. Before Boralumugheil died, his blood fused with the tears passing on some of his power of light and dark. The shards sat on the ground and when the ground melted from the new spring, they each grew into a flower. Freymiss then went into exile.

These are the first generation born of the combination of the dragon's breath

The first generation gods generated by the dragon's breath grew to many. They themselves procreated to form many more generations of gods. These children of the dragons each had their own domain on Deluvia.

It was the trickster god, Milupi, that deceived the dragons into a 10,000,000 januul sleep.

Thus began the Age of Gods

Boralumugheil’s wife is **Sophgritus** comes from the southern jungle lands and is goddess of the winds, which is why her children are now keepers of that trait. **Finnwyl**, her granddaughter, went to Sophgritus’ homelands and now occupies the Jungle Temple, the center of the world, and where the gods met the first mortals (purportedly by those that live there and follow Finnwyl). Nemistri holds power at the Tree of the Wood, and Finnwyl of the center of Song Tide, but much of their power has been relinquished to the Age of Kings(aka Age of Mortals).

## The Age of Kings (or The Age of Mortals or The Third Age) \- *24,000 januul (present time)*

Two events that happen at the end of the Second Age are the Great War between the Gods and the Mortals, and the Great Severing, a plague born of mortal discord. The World was broken

### The Great War (the war for Deluvia)

The mortals inherited from the Dragons, their magic. The Gods had their own power of miracles which they used to keep mortals as their subjects, but this power was much different than the power of magic. The old arcane arts of magery could tap into all aspects of Deluvia herself to manipulate and wield. 

The wise Dragon race decided to keep magery from the Gods, but being their children, the Gods could still manipulate areas of their own influence (e.g. a sea god could manipulate the sea), and most Gods had the ability to bless their acolytes with health or riches, or curse them with disease. Since magery could tap into all elements of Deluvia, the Gods had become jealous of the mortals and disdain formed between the two.   
It was Zweihanar who planted seeds in the other Gods minds to limit the mortals access to magic so they could be the most powerful in Deluvia. They brought disasters and pestilence against the mortals. The Gods created the Wild Skies, a barrier between the Deluvic sphere and the aether sphere so that the mortals could not study the astros and gain more wisdom and power.  
It was also the trickster/messenger god Ratatoskel that stirred up bad blood between the Gods and the Mortals, which brought about the war. The Gods were offended that the Mortals were building towers to reach the Cloud Sea top realms, but it really hurt them when they built the first airship to fly in the realm that they considered their own, private sacred space. Zweihanar struck down the first airship of Gearheed Ninnybruck called the *Aetherwing*. The location where his wreckage went down is considered a secular holy site, which is difficult to get to considering it in one of the old realms of the gods strongholds, Frostwynn. The icy weather also makes it difficult.  
It was ironically the later technologies of the airships, among other reasons, that eventually subdued the gods.

Some of the Gods did not participate on the side of the Gods and helped the mortals. This minority was led by Pallas. Other Gods that sided with Pallas were Anona, Aethera, Tresola, Embreas and Sifaneus and many of the demigods. These god’s assistance were a huge help turning the tide of the war in the Mortals favor. And it worked out for these allying gods, since in the end, they are now the highest in the Mortals pantheon.

Some of the mortals fought on the side of the Gods in this war. They were the Frost Trolls, some factions of Goblins, Endaurs, Gargoyles and some various factions such as the Jutrollag Union Brotherhood. This did not work out well for these races in the end and they exiled themselves to the far reaches of Deluvia far away from The Central Kingdoms and Song Tide.

The Gods plan backfired on them, as the mortals, needing to survive this war, turned even more to magery to dispel the Gods back. Another large reason for the armistice was a new factor and a rising force of Druvvenrog. Druvvenrog had invested heavily in new technologies, such as airships and it were these weapons that helped drive back the Gods.

It was only a few years after the War was finished that the waters rose from all sides and the rains poured  until Deluvia was covered with water. The hour when Deluvia’s Foundations fled and the firmament was ripped

Those that sided with the gods lost. How could this be with all of their omnipotence and benevolence? Clerics say that the gods turned their backs on man and allowed the will of Deluvia to decide their own fate. 

### Before the War. Mortals ascent \- *21,000 januul*

Man also got proud and thought they were smarter than the gods. The Twelve Sages  (12 Anthoran of special birth) brought magic of the Dragons back  and man chose to use magic to be as equal as the gods. Now man uses both magic and religion as powerful forces for evil and for good.   
The Twelve Elder Sages hold the physical world together with their combined virtues. They imbue their virtues into objects in the physical world that can manifest themselves into abilities and knowledge.  
Travelers in Deluvia can obtain knowledge of the virtues of the Elder Sages by making a pilgrimage to one of the Elder Sages. Each pilgrimage is fraught with danger as each Sage secludes themselves and purposely makes themselves difficult to locate to test the will and worthiness of each pilgrim.  
The Twelve Sages were the creators gods gift to the races as the end of the Second Age dwindled to provide their virtues from themselves onto the next progeny. Only the three original creator gods participated in which is why it is a direct line to them, and other virtues exist from the whole pantheon that are not listed here.

The Twelve Sages:  
**The First:** The first to come into the Third Age. The conceiver of Knowledge. His Deluvic name is Vorishba  
**The Aggressor:** The first to strike and see opportunity. The wielder of physical power and cunning to gain territory for their fellow clan.  
**The Cleric:** Seeks balance through transformation and commune with gods. Her name is Sylwyn  
**The Leader:** Holds power to sway their fellowkind to greatness in battle and to govern.  
**The Judge:** Finds fairness through discernment \- The Law Giver  
**The Free Spirit:** Not beholden to any other law. Finds strength in serendipity.  
**The Warrior:** Has skill in battle and tactics.  
**The Prosperous One:** Has much land and coin.  
**The Scholar:** The holder of knowledge from books. (His Deluvic name is Meruk)  
**The Merchant:** The crafter and seller of goods. Makes good deals.  
**The Transformer:** Transmuter of physical substances  
**The Consumer:** Hungry for information and resources and the spark of existence.

During the Age of Man, 3 of the 12 Sages, during their wanderings, came across the 3 goddess flowers, and each picked and took one for themselves. When they found their resting place and planted the flowers, they bloomed into women goddesses. Each of the 3 women took the 3 Sages for their husband. They were Falthori, Seydna, and Calnora.  
Falthori married The Free Spirit begat Charn, Bristor, Epleyna  
Seydna married The Scholar begat Seritipi, Finnwyl, Nemistri  
Calnora married The Transformer begat  Malfisis, Dalmisis, Brumisis

From all of these were born the beings that would become the first of the Age of Kings. All the children rose to greatness at some point but it was Seritipi whose realm held over to the age of mortals. That is to say, her land of Frostwynn is the only land that is intact, just as it was during the Age of Gods and not altered or destroyed by the war between the gods and man.

They built kingdoms and one such kingdom which would become the central city called Pallamost. Their god, Zweihanar was planning on taking over the rest of the gods.Pallas put a stop to this with the help of the Twelve Sages. The Twelve Sages fled from Pallamost to prevent this but the gods put a curse on Deluvia and and the Wild Skies poured rain and covered Pallamost and all of the kingdom in water.  The war between Pallas and Zweihanar left battle scars across Deluvia. Some have become sacred to either Pallas’ or Zweihanar’s acolytes. The Twelve Sages spread across  Deluvia, to high points to stay above the flood waters, and to keep watch over the gods so that they would not come back to overpower man.   
Though Pallamost’s kingdom was mostly covered in water from the great Deluge, the temple to Pallas remained on top of the highest mountain. The Pallamostian’s thought this a great sign and still worship Pallas as the greatest in their pantheon.  New Pallamost, which it is called now, is considered the strongest city of worship and protection of the gods. Many clerics seek pilgrimage to the temple to Pallas.

One far off colony of Pallamost, also survived The Great Deluge. This small mining and fishing town was called Druvenrog, for its founder, Aldvader Grimstok the Druv. Aldvader developed a special hatred for House Azernaths, the family of kings of New Pallamost, after Jom Azernath IV sent him on  a scouting mission to develop a new colony. Grimstok never reported back and vowed to conquer the Azernath kings and all of Pallamost.

Aldavar Grimstok the Druv, a Nemedi was determined to unify the disparate Nemedi clans, and the even more estranged sibling race of the Formoris, an oppressed race for their strength, they were stolen as slaves to use in other empires.   
Two long separated siblings of races, the **Nemedi** and the **Formori** joined forces against Pallamost because of their antipathy for the gods, especially the god Pallas. The Nemedi  
 The Blackcoats, as the Nemedi are called during this Civil war,

# The History of Druvvenrog 

## (Druv and Venrog)

## Notovenrog Vendradi

The Wilderness Campaign  
Terrorists  
Precogs  
Rubble  
Reconstruction  
Heap  
The mines  
The diggers  
Phaophet  
Dellatrune  
Every child in Druvenrog has heard this tale before.  
Jillicut Sisterhood

Druvenrog is the name of the group of islands now owned by The Corporate Dominion. It wasn’t always that way. 400 years ago, it started as a burgeoning fishing village that was one of the many colonies of Pallamost. After the Great Cataclysm, the great kingdom of Pallamost was in upheaval and confusion, and they retreated to their central capitol leaving the colonies to themselves. Many of the colonies were lost to the deluge, and many others succumbed to the barbarians on the outer rim. Druvenrog was fortunate to be high in the mountains and was able to escape most of the effects of the deluge.   
Druvenrog was only the name of the first town established and this is why the whole confederation of guilds on the planet still refer to the collective whole as Druvenrog. It is actually three major islands of Dregno, Merismeet and Krylla as well as some minor islands. A few mining towns popped up on all the different shores of the three islands, and in the beginning, they were in competition with one another. There was a contest to see which guild could expand the fastest and claim the most land and resources. Druvenrog was rich with ore, lumber and other resources giving the greedy, everything they needed.

* Aldvader Grimstok the Druv, [^2]started working his claim on the eastern shore and founded the village of Druvenrog on the island of Merismeet. His grandson, Ladd Grimstock III now runs the guild. Grimstok, the Elder, (the grandfather called Grimstok Aldvader) still lives in his upper castle advising his grandson.  
* Choru Duthmor starting working his claim on the northern shore and founded the village of Dunt Tallow Bay on the island of Merismeet. His grandson Broz Duthmor  now runs the guild.  
* Matssor Arcasi starting working his claim on the western shore on the island of Dregno. His grandson Genssor Arcasi now runs the guild.  
* Maney Germoonth started working his claim on the southern shore and founded the village of Hergestine on the minor island of Helog. Due to his species living longer than most, he is still running the organization  
* Elmrif Tarkon \- started working his claim on the northern shore and founded the village of Daemmelport on the island of Merismeet. His grandson, Elmrif Tarkon III now runs the guild.  
* Dryzini Biniscot was from Shimaantanople and the michithyoqua species of Gillaquid. She named her town Grazainisco. He started working his claim on the southern shore and founded the city of Grazainisco on the island of Krylla. His granddaughter Kryllic Biniscot now runs the guild.

The leader of a House is called A Gog, or The Gog (e.g. Gog Grimstok)

Mostly cabals

The purges; unholy terror  
The reign of terror, “rain” of terror He is the rainmaker

It was these 5 that banded together to form the Council of Druvenrog. These 5 Houses would be called The Five and form the core of Druvenrog politics. They all had common values that were disdain for Pallamost, no love for the gods, and to build the greatest civilization in Deluvia.

Each of the families grew in competition of one another and tried to destroy each other at first. But then they realized the House Pallamost would come back once the kingdom was recovered from the calamity of the Cataclym and they realized that they could become more powerful if they allied together. So they created the Articles of Agreement which would commercially bind them together as one Corporation. Each guild family had their own business needs in mind and would equally send representatives to The Corporation Council to decide how best to rule the affairs of their interests. Each guild would mostly control what happens in their own borders but would band together for defense and set price controls coming in and out of Druvenrog. Each year one of the six guilds would elect a Chairman to break any ties and lend general leadership.

Over the years rivalries flared up between the Guilds and the petty bickering allowed some new ones to enter The Corporation. They are considered the Lower Guilds.

Monnothonian Guild \- airship manufacturer  
	President Teedle the Repaler  
Begeron Guild \- casino operator, shipping and transport  
	Telason Treer is the administrator  
Nimmodius Guild \- airship manufacturer  
	Falk Bylglord  
Gronosial Guild \- spice mining  
	Gynomo Poxron  
Flamigor Guild  \- weapons manufacturer  
	Beed of Samsog

Each of the Lower Guilds has a significant business on Druvenrog which is why they are allowed to be on The Corporation Council. Each has a guild hall and some territory, but not nearly as significant as the Upper Guilds. They contribute a half vote and can never send up a Chairman. They can however, send up a Vice Chairman for a half-vote.

The Doxy, is the code of Druvenrog ideals, mostly the articles of corporation.

Neogardia Settlement is the island that the Formori have been relocated to after the Nemedi settled on their other lands.   
Since the Nemedi’s colonized the land of their brothers, the Formori, the Formoris have been relegated to their islands in the south and are permitted to come to the main island to work in the factories and then are shuttled back to Neogardia. There are near constant skirmishes throughout Druvenrog between the Formori and the Nemedi’s Blackcloaks.

Druvenrog is now a  powerful trading center in which families vie with each other and shift alliances for political control. The Council of Druvenrog, which is the confederation of guilds, changed names  to The Corporation, to include all the major islands of Druvenrog Major, and all of the colonies founded around Deluvia. After The Great Deluge, contact to most of the colonies on The Outer Rim was lost. The Corporation, which prided itself as a capitalistic hegenomy.

Below the Lower Guilds are what people refer to as The Gangs of Druvenrog[^3]. These are guilds that don’t have any representation on The Corporation and usually do business illegally, outside the Articles of Agreement and price fixing. They still do, however, participate in the economy of Druvenrog in direct and indirect ways. Some want to be considered legitimate Lower Guilds someday and some are just petty thieves. The Guild Gangs compete and war among each other and form their own alliances. Many have it out for the Upper Guilds and perform espionage and sabotage of their factories. Many specialize in a certain type of trade, whether it be firefighting, goldsmithing, espionage, iron mining, or shipbuilding. These gang-guilds are what might be considered a middle class and achieve some minor wealth. Others wallow in poverty and street war.

The Noble Guild Houses:

* Arch Gog Grimstok \- the founding family of Druvenrog; a mining guild (One of The Five)  
* Gog Ritter Tarkon \- architecture and building (One of The Five)  
* Gog Commissar  Duthmorr \- Espionage and security (One of The Five)  
  Gog Baroness Biniscot \-  gold and diamond trading guild  (One of The Five)  
* StormFather Arcasi \- Air ship guild and connected to to the ancient Storm Kings (One of The Five)  
* 

The  Main Higher Guilds:

* Gog Treychon \- a shipping guild Treychon Trading Company  
* Gog Commissar  Tallow \- Ore processing guild  
* Gog Overseer Steedstoss \- Automaton guild  
* Gog Templar Shrevemakis \- a military and security guild  
* Gog Doge Dokstead \- Military, mercenaries  
* Gog Prince Monnothrot \- Prison and military lower guild  
* Lady Gog Begeron \- poisons and potions and elixers; casino operator, shipping and transport Lower guild  
* Gog Nimmodius \- airship manufacturer lower guild  
* Gog Daimyo Gronisial \- spice mining lower guild  
* Gog Viceroy Flamigor \- Forging and mining \- lower guild  
* Gog Chancellor Germooth \- Horographilogists (Germooth Agency is a science guild conducting secret experiments) government test subjects. There are also secret cults following the horographilogists.

* Ichor graft \- a type of bionic/cybernetic augmentations done by the Horogromancers

All of these Guilds form what is called The Corporation. The Corporation runs all things on Druvenrog and have formed a law enforcement force called The Security Enforcement Patrol Apparatus (The secpats or the brownclads). Over the generations this has been shortened to secpats as slang. Each family contributes some soldiers to form these troops.

Druvenrog is also home to thousands of gangs that run outside of the law. Things are far too complicated for the Five and secpats to monitor or quash the gangs. Each city and district has their own turf wars going on and The Security Enforcement Patrol Apparatus (The secpats or the brownclads) seems to be able to do little about it. There is a sense of pride that each gang has, each with their own banner, colors and officers. There is a lot of respect among the gangs for a code of honor, which is different from the main culture, because they disobey the law. Some are directly related to worker's unions or crafting guilds that offer protection to each other, smuggle goods, have religious undertones and have various other crime syndicates, but they have been known to have alliances among each other from time to time. Some ask why The Security Enforcement Patrol Apparatus let this all go on, and the answer is that they will disappear deep in the subterranean tunnels and sewers and are hard to locate. The other answer is that many of the wealthier gangs pay off The Security Enforcement Patrol Apparatus, with ties that go all the way to the top.  
Some of the prominent gangs are listed below. (note: there are too many to keep track of and this is all that is available from the chroniclers)  
The major cities of Druvenrog and their gangs

Northtop is the highest peak and one of few access points through Wildspace into Kapasia, a land of floating islands. The other mountain range is called Hergestine. Hergestine has Gozon buried within it, and the Forge of the Mountain King, one of the dwarven enclaves on Druvenrog.

Druvenrog is the home of all races and represents a good cross-section from across Deluvia. The largest population of dwarves in Deluvia resides in Underdeep. Though the gargoyles have been exiled, The Goblin King Aleighgazor (and his twin, Teshgil) ‘s band of goblin refugees have found home in Gozon. Golgime is the largest commercial district in Deluvia and is home to the most diverse races and highest population density. Skirmishes erupt often, but are quickly quelled. Golgime is also known for its strict militia presence on the island by the Corporation's own Law Machine. Dunsbay Tallow is one of the most technologically enabled towns on Druvenrog, but there is also a great disparity between rich and poor and the economic caste system is alive and apparent. The dock and factory workers have resorted to living near the factories in which they work, which is mostly in lower Golgime and Krucikruss Rookery, and the living conditions can sometimes be dismal and crime, high.

Druvenrog slang:

*  a Jakker is someone who is good at using technology for their own malevolent purposes;   
* skrapper is a tinkerer who can make their own make-shift inventions from parts they "found" and scavenge   
* Skiffrunner \- a small water craft for racing and smuggling goods small distances  
* Garks \- The gangs’ name for the House nobles  
* Krats (aka Kratters) \- The gangs’ name for the House nobles  
* Patter \- a merchant  
* Grifter \- a swindler  
* Brownclads (or TBrownclads) \- The Security Enforcement Patrol Apparatus  
* Gin tuner \- a mechanic of skiff runners  
* A Ginner \- a racher of a skiff runner

Aguygent Prowgnaw  
A Chronicler writes  
A thousand ships with a thousand cargoes are being unladen every week; and not only is every package of this vast and varied merchandise picked up and set down accurately but each is weighed and opened; sampled and recorded and again, stitched up and laid in its place, without haste or waste or hurry or confusion by a very few men in short sleeves; who working with the utmost organization in the common interest are yet able to pause in their work and say to the casual visitor, would you like to see what sort of thing we find in sacks of cinnamon? Look at this snake\!'

* 

The Lower class are all the workers in the factories, the service industry and all the poor people that don’t have jobs. Life can be dismal and unhealthy for them, from the putrid water, to the hazy polluted air. Conditions in the factories are not safe either. This group makes up fifty percent of the population of Druvenrog. Many are new immigrants looking to find new fortune in this city of opportunity.

By the end of the first generation of settlers the villages became cities and the borders started to get close to butting up against one another. Thankfully the Articles of Agreement handled who got what. Upstart guilds would wedge in between any open territory. Cities would build up into the sky and down into the dirt to gain more territory.

During the second generation it was decided to build a canal system in and through Druvenrog. Each city was responsible for its own portion, which lead to no universal system of travel. This still greatly improved travel throughout Druvenrog, but was disorganized.  It was at the end of this generation that two great discoveries were made, The Great Forge, and The Northtop Passage.

The Great Forge is deep down in the bottom of the stone and dirt, but it was a fire that seemed to never burn out and burned hotter than any fire ever seen. It was magical. The Corporation harnessed this energy for even greater forging of materials and built a structure around it to limit its use from outsiders.

The Northtop Passage is small opening in the Wild Skies that leads to more open skies above. The Wild Skies, a layer of clouds and storms that wraps the planet and doesn’t allow anyone or anything to pass through. This one unique area on top of Northtop Mountain was a break and allowed for new opportunity for exploration. Here they discovered the lost race of Kapasian Elves, that were lost to Deluvia one thousand years ago. This is where the Druvenrog expansion up would stop, as they feared the Elves and formed a treaty to leave them alone.

Over the course of the second generation, The Corporation formed The Security Enforcement Patrol Apparatus (TBrownclads). A group of elite soldiers that would police the islands and as well as the coastline. They would crack down on the gangs and try to keep prices intact. They root out gangs and keep marauders and pirates at bay. 

With all of the new found riches and success, The Corporation got greedy and turned its back on magic. The Security Enforcement Patrol Apparatus was entrusted to stop its usage and an elite group of The Security Enforcement Patrol Apparatus, known as The Inquisitors, became mage hunters and hunted down any remaining mages and slaughtered them calling magery a heretical impurity. The only power The Corporation wanted on their island was the power of commerce. Indeed Druvenrog was now rich and powerful. They had no need for magic or religion. All of the shrines and temples were shut down and converted into shops, offices or factories. 

Now at the end of the third generation, a new technology of airship travel has been invented allowing travel to far off lands especially up to Kapasia in the Wild Space. New trade routes can be established which is desperately needed for Druvenrog as they have no more space for lumber or for farming. They need to import so much wood and food to keep building their structures and feeding their people.

The third generation of Guild leaders is aging and ready for a new brand of leaders. There is much pressure coming from everywhere  threatening their existence; from the far off Demons wanting to rule the world, the pirates on The Long Sea raiding trade routes, new upstart empires from the Outer Rim, New Pallamost wanting to regain their former glory, and rot from within.

Druvenrog and The Corporation do seem to be the most powerful regime of the Central Kingdoms during current time. New Pallamost still has its highly trained army and The Kingdom of the Wood has power in magic but airship travel give Druvenrog a huge edge.

Cast in Druvenrog:  
Bander \- member of a small upstart gang called the Corvidroods. A hopeful ginner  
Kataryss \- member of a small upstart gang called the Corvidroods. A hopeful firekeeper  
Trale \- member of a small upstart gang called the Corvidroods. A hopeful airship captain

Skrin \- a skrapper that is friends with Bander

High Inquisitor Drollfrot \- Hunts magery users to bring them to trial for heresy in the Court of the Kom. He stays mostly in the Central Kingdoms region  
High Inquisitor Drumizid \- Hunts mages on the outer rim.  
Marshall Treyfrill \- leader of a band of Brownclads that is given its own autonomy to weed out and infiltrate gangs in the underdeep.   
Admiral Briffrin \- airship captain, leader of the air navy

#### Terms:

**Skrappers** are merchants that roam the Long Sea for derelict craft and take what they find useful to sell in the cities.   
**patter** is any merchant, a shopkeep  
**skamper** is pretty much the same thing as a skrapper but probably less knowledgeable about what they're selling. That is, a skamper doesn't go out on the Long Sea to do the salvage, but stays on land to just try to make a quick coin  
**gin tuner** works on skiffrunner to try to make it faster and faster to compete in the nightly races in the canals. a few of skrappers are also gin tuners, which has them save some of the best junk for themselves.  
**Ginner** \- a skiffrunner racer  
**Gravver** \- farmers who try to terraform land on the Long Sea. They do this primarily with kelp and are kelp farmers.

**Garks** \- a colloquial term for a business man. One of the factory owners  
**Krats** \- a colloquial term for a high official. Gang members call the Houses this.  
**Brownclads** \- a colloquial term short for The Security Enforcement Patrol Apparatus

## The Founding of Druvenrog

Aldvader Grimstok the Druv was sent by Jom Azernath IV of Pallamost to found a new colony. Grimstok was part of of the Pallatian Council and had ambitions of his own. He went the opposite direction he was ordered to go until he came upon a group of islands he named Druvenrog after his kind, the Druvs, a subgroup of Nemedi,. Along with Grimstok was Uftan the Good, Surtyrbrok, Sithoan Freeg, Yome Yordok, and a group of marines for military support. They all decided together, to break ties with Pallamost and form their own empire.   
**Grimstok** despised the gods for their pettiness. He wanted to start a civilization that was free of the gods, and had their own free will.

The island he settled, he called Merismeets, because of the River Meris, Meris being his wife’s name, and where the river meets The Long Sea.

Soon after, Broz **Duthmorr** landed upon the shores of what was now called Druvenrog. Duthmorr, a fellow Anthoran, but of the Rood clan, which had rat-like form. Duthmorr had like values and also disliked the gods so him and Grimstok formed a close friendship. 

Another settler that came was Genssor **Arcasi**, about 1 year after Grimstok arrived. Arcasi was from a far off land and of a race called the Nemedi. He landed on the western shores on an island that he called Dregno, after an old Nemedi god. 

At about the same time, Elmrif **Tarkon**, an administrator from the Old Pallamost, also seeking refuge from the imperialism and self-piety of Pallamost. He named the city he claimed Daemmelport. Tarkon was half Elfinfolk and half Otaur Anthoran.

Krylic **Biniscot** landed upon the southern island of Krylla (named after herself), she was from Shimaantanople and the michithyoqua species of Gillaquid. She named her town Grazainisco.

It was these 5 that banded together to form the Council of Druvenrog. These 5 Houses would be called The Five and form the core of Druvenrog politics. They all had common values that were disdain for Pallamost, no love for the gods, and to build the greatest civilization in Deluvia.

They all knew that they were in competition with one another, but that they also had to work together to grow stronger than Pallamost. These Families vie for control over Druvenrog and the balance goes back and forth.

## Druvenrog today

Maintain order and restore prosperity 

Druvenrog is now a  powerful trading center in which families vie with each other and shift alliances for political control. The Council of Druvenrog, which is the confederation of guilds, changed names  to The Corporation, to include all the major islands of Druvenrog Major, and all of the colonies founded around Deluvia. After The Great Deluge, contact to most of the colonies on The Outer Rim was lost. The Corporation, which prided itself as a capitalistic hegenomy.

The Noble Guild Houses (Metabarons):

* Arch Gog Grimstok \- the founding family of Druvenrog; a mining guild (One of The Five)  
* Gog Ritter Tarkon \- architecture and building (One of The Five)  
* Gog Commissar  Duthmorr \- Espionage and security (One of The Five)  
  Gog Baroness Biniscot \-  gold and diamond trading guild  (One of The Five)  
* StormFather Arcasi \- Air ship guild and connected to to the ancient Storm Kings (One of The Five)  
* 

The  Main Higher Guilds:

* Gog Treychon \- a shipping guild Treychon Trading Company  
* Gog Commissar  Tallow \- Ore processing guild  
* Gog Overseer Steedstoss \- Automaton guild  
* Gog Templar Shrevemakis \- a military and security guild  
* Gog Doge Dokstead \- Military, mercenaries  
* Gog Prince Monnothrot \- Prison and military lower guild  
* Lady Gog Begeron \- poisons and potions and elixers; casino operator, shipping and transport Lower guild  
* Gog Nimmodius \- airship manufacturer lower guild  
* Gog Daimyo Gronisial \- spice mining lower guild  
* Gog Viceroy Flamigor \- Forging and mining \- lower guild  
* Gog Chancellor Germooth \- Horographilogists (Germooth Agency is a science guild conducting secret experiments) government test subjects. There are also secret cults following the horographilogists.

* Ichor graft \- a type of bionic/cybernetic augmentations done by the Horogromancers

All of these Guilds form what is called The Corporation. The Corporation runs all things on Druvenrog and have formed a law enforcement force called The Security Enforcement Patrol Apparatus. Over the generations this has been shortened to secpats as slang. Each family contributes some soldiers to form these troops.

Druvenrog is also home to thousands of gangs that run outside of the law. Things are far too complicated for the Five and Brownclads to monitor or quash the gangs.Each city and district has their own turf wars going on and The Security Enforcement Patrol Apparatus seems to be able to do little about it. There is a sense of pride that each gang has, each with their own banner, colors and officers. There is a lot of respect among the gangs for a code of honor, which is different from the main culture, because they disobey the law. Some are directly related to worker's unions or crafting guilds that offer protection to each other, smuggle goods, have religious undertones and have various other crime syndicates, but they have been known to have alliances among each other from time to time. Some ask why The Security Enforcement Patrol Apparatus let's this all go on, and the answer is that they will disappear deep in the subterranean tunnels and sewers and are hard to locate. The other answer is that many of the wealthier gangs pay off The Security Enforcement Patrol Apparatus, with ties that go all the way to the top.  
Some of the prominent gangs are listed below. (note: there are too many to keep track of and this is all that is available from the chroniclers)

**Underdeep** \- A loose grouping of underground factories, mining towns and tunnels hollowed out under Northtop Mountain. No one really knows everything that's down there and it's impossible to map out. The gangs run wild down there. Too many gangs to count.  
Underdeep Troupers

**Gozon** \- a section of Underdeep that is designated for the Goblin clan. It was gifted to the goblins for their refuge and is now technically a pene-exclave region. Gozon has many districts. There are huge factories, forges, refineries and more that the goblins have fitted for their tinkering skill to create some unique goods sought among Deluvians.

**Fogwryhta Heights** \- A residential district and steam engine factory above Krucikruss Rookery

**Fire Triangle** \- A center of forges that is forever burning

**Dane's Crucible** \- The main forge of Fire Triangle (aka The Great Forge)

Army of the Changing World

The Mage Trials

Northtop is the highest peak and one of few access points through Wildspace into Kapasia, a land of floating islands. The other mountain range is called Hergestine. Hergestine has Gozon buried within it, and the Forge of the Mountain King, one of the dwarven enclaves on Druvenrog.

Druvenrog is the home of all races and represents a good cross-section from across Deluvia. The largest population of dwarves in Deluvia resides in Underdeep. Though the gargoyles have been exiled, The Goblin King Aleighgazor (and his twin, Teshgil) ‘s band of goblin refugees have found home in Gozon. Golgime is the largest commercial district in Deluvia and is home to the most diverse races and highest population density. Skirmishes erupt often, but are quickly quelled. Golgime is also known for its strict militia presence on the island by the Corporation's own Law Machine. Dunsbay Tallow is one of the most technologically enabled towns on Druvenrog, but there is also a great disparity between rich and poor and the economic caste system is alive and apparent. The dock and factory workers have resorted to living near the factories in which they work, which is mostly in lower Golgime and Krucikruss Rookery, and the living conditions can sometimes be dismal and crime, high.

Druvenrog slang:

*  a Jakker is someone who is good at using technology for their own malevolent purposes;   
* skrapper is a tinkerer who can make their own make-shift inventions from parts they "found" and scavenge   
* Skiffrunner \- a small water craft for racing and smuggling goods small distances  
* Garks \- The gangs’ name for the House nobles  
* Krats (aka Kratters) \- The gangs’ name for the House nobles  
* Patter \- a merchant  
* Grifter \- a swindler  
* Secpats (or TBrownclads) \- The Security Enforcement Patrol Apparatus Gin tuner \- a mechanic of skiff runners  
* A Ginner \- a racer of a skiff runner

A Chronicler writes  
A thousand ships with a thousand cargoes are being unladen every week; and not only is every package of this vast and varied merchandise picked up and set down accurately but each is weighed and opened; sampled and recorded and again, stitched up and laid in its place, without haste or waste or hurry or confusion by a very few men in short sleeves; who working with the utmost organization in the common interest are yet able to pause in their work and say to the casual visitor, would you like to see what sort of thing we find in sacks of cinnamon? Look at this snake\!'

In the main current story line, Druvvenrog is pursuing imperialism and colonization and even hopes of ruling all of Deluvia and exporting its values to all of Deluvia.This would include extinguishing magic and religion. They are also experimenting with ichor tech that is actually extracting the blood of hibernating dragons far below in the core of Deluvia (they don’t know they are dragons, they think the dragons are a myth and/or long extinct)

Exodus Stronghold  
(Exod Arcem)  
The settlers were making their way east to escape the wars and disasters trying to create a new life away from the Central Kingdoms  
Exodus Stronghold was the first outpost built in the east but was quickly overrun by bandits that have lived in the outlands for many years before.  
Once and while a new set of settlers will try to keep the island as a home

Padula Anchorite  
(this can be a potential starting location)  
The Padula acolytes also founded the Padula Anchorite a small recluse but recently turned to a market and stationed with a few guard to fight off bandits. It was thought that the Padula monks had been wiped out by bandits but a merchant came across the anchorite and found that they were still alive and well. Somehow a market was allowed on the lower tier of the outcrop. The Padulas withdrew to their small monastery on the higher levels of the outcrop. They allowed the merchants to come and go as they realized that they could not survive entirely by themselves, as now a few guards were always present to protect the merchants, the goods and even themselves. No one is allowed to talk to them, and they are rarely seen. Some chroniclers write that the Padulas were worshippers of the dragons and went out to the eastern outlands to wait for their return.   
One secret to them repelling the bandits, is the steep walls of their small island make it easy to defend. The guards that are maintained on the island do a great job at keeping attackers at bay. One might  wonder why they are so elite to protect such a small, nondescript rock in the middle of The Long Sea. 

Friar Wover  
Abbot Dreer  
Prior Sleegs  
Friar Dicant  
Friar Sigfint  
They are all clerics of medium power and a member of their own guild of gnomish tinkers called the Padula Anchorites. They worship the God Talluk in their small chapel.  
The build small parts (parts for clocks, locks, they don’t know what they end up being used for, but their order has always been craftsmen)  that they trade with other ports across The Long Sea.   
Talluk is the patron god of craftsmanship and is sympathetic to Mortals and offers blessings. He often is a patron god of gnomes, dwarfs and goblins, and of tinkers, blacksmiths and other crafters. His acolytes seem to always be industrious, practical and frugal.  
Even the Padulas like to keep to themselves and guard the secrets of their guild. They don’t do their business in the market at the base of their Abbey, but rather separately in ships that come at different times, and mostly with Rothigport.  
This order does not intend on growing any bigger, but since Prior Sleegs is near the end of his aging life, they do seek to replenish their numbers to stay at a group of 5 eventually.  
They observe the market below, without anyone knowing, looking for potential candidates to join their ranks. All three of, Wover, Dicant and Sigfint want to be promoted to Prior after Dreer passes.   
The candidate must be a cleric already seeking the wisdom of Talluk. Though the brotherhood will teach the new acolyte the necessary spells and tinker skills, they send potentials off on quests to test their worth.

One of their secrets is that they are hiding a Formori princess that has escaped from the mines of Didolmauz where her people are imprisoned. Her enslavers, The Pallamosts are searching for her, so it is important that this secret is kept. This is too far away from the Pallamost homeland for them to be too worried.  
The new acolyte must also keep this secret and help in this cause.

# Song Tide

Song Tide is one of the ancient lands not yet touched by the new. It is a combination of the old domains gods and of magic. It is one of the few strongholds of magic which has all but been vanquished from the rest of Deluvia by the Central Kingdoms of Pallamost and Druvenrog.  
It can be found on the western edge of the wilderness and on the outer fringe of the civilized kingdoms.   
Geography:  
Song Tide is a grouping of islands.   
**Noctisbard** is the most populated island and, in the North central area. Gargium Channel is to the east. Goylsmuth Bay is to the east where Rothigport, the largest town in Song Tide is. The Omphalos is also here. On the south area of Notisbard is the Sanctuary shrine to the fairy goddess Wispa  Mynia- of lilac fairies

**Rystrilmyl** is the second largest island and is located in Western Song Tide. It is so named because of the swamp that is on the Eastern side of the island.  On the west side of the island, in the middle of the forest is the small stone-towered town of **Magewood**, which is now called **Pippinsnest** since the Raven Clan has taken it as their home land. From their leader Pippin  
On the western driftless gorges is the Mage Guild town called Anona’s Oasis and also the Tomb of God  Anona (the third king) and his cult resides here. On the North central coast is the town of **Runesbrook**, a commune of glyph scribes, looking into the deep mysteries of the Deluvic language. Many know that Runeload Hepstupitan has a shop here where adventurers can learn the craft of rune marking and much more. The Glyphics and Runelords are able to etch runes and imbue and extract magic from them, especially travel and time magic.  
**Migreelamyre** is a bog that is the southern part of Rystrilmyl. The Mandagoras is on the Eastern side of the island.

**Roolpellikarta**  
Is the land around the mermaid and pirate town.  
The eastern side of the island is the home of the Badger clan and they call that area the Bent Buggle Burrows

**Dergheim** is the largest island of the Song Tide In the far east of the Geistgor Mountains is **Bristlechill Keep** the home of **Ukra Ospirion**, a baroness tinker. **Nax Hollum** lives in **Raxelcroft** on this island just southeast of Rothigport.  
In the center is Requilly Moors and the small town of **Lullyfort**.   
	Lullyfort nestled at the foot of the Geistgor Mountains, considers themselves Shepherd of the Requilly Moors, that it overlooks. The original builders of this town were the Mice Clan so many of its residents are still that, but many other creatures inhabit Lullyfort and dozens of pilgrims come through each day given its location near many interesting destinations.  
The Guild of Shepherds keeps monsters and marauders at a minimum, so most travelers through the Moors can feel safe.  
Goylstone River runs east out of the bay from Rothigport and leads up the Geistgor Mountains into the Bristlechill peaks. At the top and source of the river is a cave that leads down to the Glistelgeth Caverns where the entrance to the Dirt Kingdom is.  
**Mideluviput** is the fourth largest island and towns of **Hawk Finster Hollow** and **Thistle Hymn** are located here.  
**Dreglematia** is a large island in the south of Song Tide that contains the mage tower of **Reg Therox**  the wizard of the lake. Dregor Lake  
**Chantwood Isle** is fifth largest island and the small town of Minwood Snag in the tree valley land of Fernfullow Vale  
 Henz Riggleboot  
	Characters: Francis Tuckles, Brinstly Boggs, Archer Demmins, Swilly Fisher  
Francis Tuckles lives in Bentbuggle Burrows and has never ventured far off this little lush island of Chantwood. He lets the adventures come to him. In the evenings he is the lead lute player in his band The Wailing Banshees at Tallytuck Pub. During the day he wanders around the island finding valuables that he sells to adventurers that he crosses paths with.  
Being Badger Clan has its advantages as he uses his adept digging skills to find treasures beneath the island mountains. He is not too shabby with staff weapons, his favorite being his Bō, and he'll use it when he is grumpy and gets in a quarrel, or to defend the honor of an insulted bar maiden at the pub, which is far too often the burrowfolk will tell you.  
**Ildaria** is an island,and the home of **Timistrius**, the gardener wizard and her Ildarian Gardens, and the location of one of the ancient Ildarian Guardians of the Song Tide.  
**Volykragulon** is the island of the volcano in Song Tide. The sorceress **Orta Vollim** lives on the south side of the island. She is one of the Four Archmages  
**Nismrit** is a small island in Western Song Tide and home to **Voluk Nissrut** the mage and herbalist, one of the Four Archmages

**Lalfyn**  
**Gailyth**

**Scarburry \- the pirate town**

**Cantosturmo (or Cantomaran)**  Bardtown is the second largest town in Song Tide and is considered the home of the bards. (although bards are in every town and in the countryside as well) It is spread across two islands Cantos and Turmo and is a town of allure and festiveness, including the amphitheater where aspiring actors and musicians can perform. Some of the most prestigious Bards in Deluvia live here. They reside in their cottages to stay close to their fans and accolytes and get inspired writing and composing by the seaside and once in a while, performing at the famous amphitheatre

Cantosturmo was founded when a merchant vessel  captained by **Kersirus** and crew was lured to the rock by the enchantress Kixie with her enthralling music. **Kixie** grandaughter of Zeyphant the Tempest, had lured many ships into the rock called Cantosturmo throughout the ages where their timbers were smashed and sunk along the shores. It was Kersirus and his shanties that changed her mind and her song and eased his ship gently into shore. There Kersus and he crew stayed on the barren rock. The crew married Kixie’s maidens and Kersirus married Kixie and they begat Manesk the Bard. **Manesk** took the best of his mother’s wailing, luring songs, and combined the aspects of his father’s sea shanties which became the spellsongs that this future town would be known for. These legends grew of the spellsongs across Deluvia, drawing chroniclers, and performers, which helped build the town.   
It also drew the attention of Meruk, one of the 12 Sages, the sage of scholars and chroniclers, for he wanted to watch, how this town would develop in preserving the lore of the world.  
Kixie the lesser but immortal goddess, moved out into the Long Sea to mourn Kersirus after his mortal death, but many still worship her. Kixie now resides east of Song Tide on a rock of The Long Sea and plays her harp, no longer luring fisherman, but playing dirges for her lost soul mate. Those that still worship her, can visit her, though they have to get through the maelstrom. Once they do, they can learn the Dirge of Kirsirus, a most ultimate melody that can bring armadas crashing down if in the wrong hands.

Bardtown is a festive town which seems to have a party somewhere in the town every night. Often the amphitheatre is the center of activity, where people gather when there is not a performance. There is also a nice garden at the top tier where bards mingle with other socialites of the town. The Greater Songtide Symphony also performs here on a regular schedule, which  that includes members from many towns across the Song Tide and beyond.  
Krizdo and is wonderwagon are often found outside the city limits on the beach as he is no longer allowed in town for the fires and havoc he’s caused. He comes back once a moontick or and some of the citizens that want to remain in contact will go down to see him.

Bardtown is the City of Harmony. And the City of Sandstone. It seeks harmony and balance in all things. It wishes to keep all the elements of Deluvia in balance with each other and not let any virtue outweigh another.

**The Gryphon** is the Inn on top of the hill. 

**The Saddle and Loom Fine Wools** is the tailor and leather armorer. Piper (fox clan) is a weaver and tailor that is almost always in need of more wool. Thorn (bear clan) is her husband and he is the leather armorer. Both can teach the skill of tailoring, but Piper can mend clothing and has a minor skill for leather if she has to, and Thorn will repair leather armor at an expert level. Piper and Thorn Wisterthimble have been running the shop for many years and have been providing the best apparel and armor in central Song Tide.   
Piper will ask you to gather her some wool for her and in return will pay you and provide you with a new sewing kit. Piper also crafts all of the linothorax armor for Thorn’s sets which need them.  
Thorn will ask you bring bring him some leather and in return will provide you with the **Musicians Satchel**, and its recipe to craft it. The satchel is a special pouch that holds reagents and materials specific to the bard.   
Both of them have better quests and rewards later on.  
The player can also buy any basic tailoring item from either of them. And these two are also experts in imbuing songspells in their armor and can set you down that path.

**The Lute and the Lyre**, is the music shop and tuner shop. **Dryope** the Tuner is the shopkeep and she will tune your harps, lyres, lutes or most any instrument, to keep it in tip-top shape.  
She will sell or buy a variety of instruments

**Cybellis the Organist** \- has been cast down to the bottom layers of the Whisperfount for the strength of her sound from his most unusual instrument. The strange storms that this column of air will produce. Now her air travels up through the central column of the library creating unusual but melodic sounds.  Her assistant **Tymp** scurries around the chambers gathering books for Cybellis to use in her arrangements.

The central chamber of the Library of the Whisperfount also holds **Pagas’ Pendulum** suspending down from the tabula phobia organum to the library bottom, through the central chamber. Pagas, part scientist of time and part musician studies the movement of the pendulum and the writings it makes as some signs from the gods for new songprayers to Kixie or Zeyphant.

**The Sodality of Bards** is the largest known association of creative arts in Deluvia and its main guild hall is in Bardtown. They are the keepers of tradition for this part of Deluvia. They work together to progress their craft and keep the ancient stories and make new ones. If they have a Grand Bardic meeting they will meet in the amphitheatre. Though they welcome all of the different studies of Bards, they specialize in the Hall of the Glossolalia, which is another way of saying they study the old Deluvic language to decipher the power in its mysteries. In the mystical script of knowledge, the adept acts as a glossator, unraveling the cryptic verses with the fervor of glossolalia, revealing hidden truths in the sacred dance of interpretation

The Conservatory of Cantosturmo is behind the stage, with study chambers and sleeping quarters for students, wishing to become a bard. This is where there is a secret passage to Whisperfount and the eventually the belltower.

They meet deep in the Whisperfount. On Whisperfounts first layer is the tabula phobia organum.   
There exists the membrane which taps into the meta-arcana, which is the vibrations and frequencies of Deluvia’s inner song.

The Five Halls, if apprenticed under, will offer new specializations to the player beyond the core Bard spellsongs

Hall of Mischance \- tragedy, sorrow and horror in drama and music  
Hall of Harlequin  \- has to do with humor and deception in music or drama  
Hall of Glossolalia \- language, speaking especially the ancient Deluvic  
Hall of Hearten \- inspiration in music  
Hall of Mythos \- writings and tradition usually epic poetry of the tribe.

Cantosturmo Bardic House “Luskala” or “The Steps” is the name of the amphitheatre that the bards make their center of activity. The Steps are used by some halls as an initiation right, for initiates to climb reciting lines or lyrics according to the Hall. This metaphor runs strong in Bardtown.

**The Six Bards** of Bardtown as they are often called; though there are more, especially aspiring musicians and poets, they are the most well-known in the realm and patronize their associated Hall. 

Ansturn Cagliostros \- a bard that has his house in Bardtown. He is called Cagliostros by all and is a legendary living poet best known for his work “The Peliziod”. 

Oghamma Triss \- a bard that has her house in Bardtown

Lucan \- a bard that has his house in Bardtown

Kleio Tamhan the thespain \- a bard that has her house in Bardtown

Dryzak Kynto \- a bard that has his house in Bardtown

Ollama Tridtrix \- a bard that has her house in Bardtown

Gilderstilt Oveeris \- The guild master for Hall of Glossolalia

A bard is also a path to the Druid class among other ways (cleric and ranger are others ).

Temple of the StormCallers \- Followers of the Tempest God, Zeyphant the Storm Lord, whose songprayers calm or stir up violent storms. Stormweavers and Stormlight  
	Many join this religion to become the title of Troubadours a cleric poet that tells and since the stories of the Awesome and Terrible power of  Zeyphant. When achieve, these Troubadours of Zeyphant evangelize Deluvia, though Zeyphant himself only resides in and around the Song Tide archipelago and rose to prominence after the War, after his mother, Vulsong was humiliated during the Great War and exiled to the Great Down Below.

**The StormCaller Belltower and Lighthouse** is a landmark used by seafarers through this central passage of Song Tide. but also as a location for initiating a bard cleric of the Stormcallers Sect, as they climb the 32 steps and recite each of the 32 songprayers to Zeyphant, 16 of which to calm storms, and 16 to surge storms. When at the top they sing their own songprayer that they had spent the last 8 januul crafting and see if Zeyphant will accept it. Some troubadours at this point, will be swept away from the winds and it is unknown if Zeyphant has thrown them into the mouth of his sister, Moskvrek, or ascended them to a prophet. 

Not to be confused with the storm magic that is the element energy, but this is the water and wind control of the gods and the prayers that draw forth the blessings or malediction.  
They have a chamber they named **Whisperfount** dug in the middle of the mountain where they preserve the knowledge of Zeyphant and the ancient Deluvic tongue which can be used in songs and prayers. There is a large library which goes far down below the mountain.  
The most prominent prophet of Zeyphant is Rastream who lives in the cleric chambers of the Whisperfount. The Library of WhisperFount is their collection of ancient Deluvic Codexes. The Stormcaller sect tend to stay out of the public and stay in the chamber writing their tombs and practice reciting their prayers.  
The regular public, that are not part of this religion don’t see much of the practitioners, except to hear their prayers come out of the belltower and feel the winds that are derived from their songs.

This is the largest sect of Stormcallers outside of the of the Cathedral of the Wind, which makes this a stop along the Galestrom’s Path, a quest for acolytes of Gods of the Wind.  
This is a path to become a Storm Paladin 

Prayers:

Devotion to Doldrums  
Quellwinds Carol

Whisperwind \- this song can carry a prayer to a friend that is far away  
Psalms of Serenity \- Slows winds and stops combat and aggro  
Intercessory Breeze \- Can remove curses from a friendly party from the god being prayed to  
Breath of Vulsong \- Bring Vulsong into battle for you  
Blessing of the Fleet \- Blesses all friendly party’s ships  
Headwinds Hymnody \- this will make your ship fast and steady  
Luckwind \-

These are all songprayers of past acolytes that have now become part of the canon and written in the **Hymnal of the Stormlord** 

Stormcallers are often employed on ships to try to calm the weather as the ship is crossing The Long Sea, or to provide a wind, when there is not one, speeding their journey		

**Krizzdo the goblin tinker magician**, travels to Bardtown once a month or so on his many rounds across the Song Tide islands with his Wonder Wagon to peddle goods and show off his latest tricks. In the beginning, Krizzdo would come all the way into Bardtown and even convinced the leading bards to let him on stage, but one evening, Krizzdo was to surprise the audience with his most amazing tricks ever. It backfired on him and the stage started on fire. (it was rebuilt to be even more magnificent) He was never allowed back in again. So when he comes he stays outside the city limits and tries to get the attention of travelers and someday, once again impress the performers of Bardtown and become one of them with his act.

Krizzdo (when first seeing the player) “hrrrmm, the wind blows in another mortal from far off lands. Can you help dearest traveler. I can make it worth your while.”

Player: “What is wrong sire?”

Krizzdo “You mock Krizzdo, but I am desperate and you seem stronger and smarter than most that pass here, so I will tell you. My wheel here is broken”

“Can you find a bolt for it lying around here? If you can and repair my wheel, I, Krizzdo the Magnificent, at your service, will give you the show of your life of anything that can be seen across all The Long Sea”

He is from Raven clan, but as a youngling, was thrown from the nest and was severely disformed and now wears a Mask of the Glossator.

**The Seven Slayer books**   
We all know there are the 7 slayer types  
\- humanoid (opposite undead)  	Location: Wraithwood Blight  
\- reptile  (opposite to arachnid)  	Location: Gilgome Desert  
        	\- undead (opposite humanoid) 	Location: Songtide Islands- Garoot’s Cabin  
        	\- fey (opposite abyss) 		Location: Duhmkaazm Abyss  
        	\- elemental (opposite all others) 	Location: Songtide Islands \- Laelaps the storm watcher  
        	\- abyss (opposite few) 		Location: Feycundia Forests  
        	\- arachnid (opposite to reptile) 	Location: Rystrilmyl Swamp

These hunter bestiaries, are tomes, with the lore gathered by Hunters (rangers) over the centuries and carry the knowledge of beasts of this type. When obtained, and studied, the hunter gains bonuses against these types. For example, if the ranger has obtained and studied the Undead Bestiary, they gain a damage bonus using ranger specialization attacks against all undead. Over time they can learn new specialization skills specific for the monster type. When using the Tracking skill, they gain a bonus when searching for that monster type.

The tome’s keepers are spread throughout Deluvia, but some lie in Song Tide.

They can be copied by scribes, but the original needs to be found by Rangers.

The first one the players are likely to encounter is at Garroots Cabin

Another source of information is Wulvern, the huntsman. He can give the Spear of the Huntsman.  
He belongs to the Fraternity of the Fleetfoot, a guild of rangers that has a mission to purge the Outlands of the Warlords that are creeping in on The Songtide. 

**Mistop Keep** a western island potion laboratory, and the domain of **Termir Mograg**, the wizard,   
Moors  
Hellstone  
Brinner Hailstork

**Snarlbush Hollow**  is the Formori[^4] village south of Noctisbard. They have been raiding routes out of Rothigport for the last few years

# The Creatures of Songtide

The overworld creatures  
Kobold (caves)  
Goblin  
Gnoll (various locations )  
	Gnoll hunter  
	Gnoll Warrior (spearman, pikeman  
	Gnoll Shaman/Cleric  
Gnoll Marauder  
It is believed by some that gnolls had traces of demonic blood, which may be evidenced by unusual features found among some of the gnoll bloodlines. These may have included talons, gleaming red eyes, or black fur with fiery orange spots.  
There are two encampments in Songtide.  The Gnolls are ferocious and sometimes raid the other towns in Song Tide, so most residents don’t get along with them. Most times the gnolls keep to themselves  
Clawfold Pack  
Mamblesnear Pack  
They are at war with each other and sometimes other towns get caught in the middle. These wars are part of their ritual so they never get too large or out of control. The other residents of Song Tide look at it as a game, as long as they don’t get caught in the middle.   
Gnolls don’t use magic, but have some religion, and their shamans can do some prayer spells.

The Feud between the two packs over hunting territory keeps some balance between them and is a tribute to their main god, **Fermangal**, a petty demi god who uses their bloody feud for his amusement.   
The player can interfere with this feud, play one side or broker a truce.  
When the player comes across a Gnoll Camp. The god they worship, Fermangal, plays tells different things to different clans to make them hate each other and garner their worship. Whichever clan worships him more, he will aid in battles against the other Clan. If the player can help them realize this, the Clans will work together, find new gods and broaden their pantheon. Fermangal will be angered and become an enemy of the player, but the player will have the Gnolls as an ally.  
	Step 1: Find all the Gnoll camps. There are 4 in each Clan spread throughout Song Tide. They are nomadic, so they travel from one to the other, in no particular order.  
In each camp, the Gnolls will not attack the player until the player attacks them. They are busy hunting and gathering and preparing war against the opposing clan. The Gnolls have no quarrel with the non-Gnolls unless they are aggressed upon.  
If they find all of one clan and attack in each camp, the opposing clan, once discovered, will talk to you in their language and give you a reward, The Talisman of Furboor. They assume you are helping them defeat the other clan. This is where the player can learn of this feud. The system keeps track of the amount of blood spilled per clan, by the player, and the more on one side will keep them in favor with the other side.

Mamblesnear \+4 || Clawfold \-4  Mamblesnear gives player Talisman of Furboor  
Mamblesnear \+3 || Clawfold \-3  
Mamblesnear \+2 || Clawfold \-2  
Mambersnear \+1 || Clawfold \-1  
Mamblesnear 0 || Clawfold 0 (neutral)  
Mamblesnear \-1 || Clawfold \+1  
Mamblesnear \-2 || Clawfold \+2  
Mamblesnear \-3 || Clawfold \+3  
Mamblesnear \-4 || Clawfold \+4   Clawfold gives player Direheen Katar

When the player is neutral or positive in one clan, that clan will no longer attack the player. But the more negative a clan is, the more all of that camp will attack you.

You can collect the pieces of a gnoll disguise from various NPCs in Song Tide. 

1. The shaman gnoll headdress (one for each clan)  
   1. The player must find a shaman from the clan and be at \+4 in that clan.  
   2. If the player is the cleric class then the shaman gives the player the headdress  
   3. If the player is a class other than a cleric, they must go through an initiation ritual  
   4. They receive a healing salve, learn the Nightmare spell for completing this.  
2. The gnoll pelt \- not much for armor, but gives frost protection and Blood Lust skill  
3. Claws of the Mongrel \- a weapon with slashing attacks and blocking abilities  
     
   Depending on which headdress is work, this will also give you one extra negative toward the other clan. With will double their aggro against you if worn in their presence.  
     
   Step 2: The shrine to Fermangal:  
   The Gnolls, when talking to the player, will mention Fermanal and the offerings, though it will be unclear with their broken common mixed with Gnollish.  
   They could also stumble upon the shrine and learn the entry point into this lore event.  
   If they come without the Gnoll disguise Fermangal will think they are of that Gnoll clan and try to manipulate the player as if they were a member of the clan. The player can then realize the deep deception that Fermangal is using to manipulate her acolytes.

   Gnolls are Song Tiders afterall and defend against any marauders that come by to pillage the islands  
     
   They are nomadic and use boats to go from island to island. They appear at a different location depending on random factors
