***Section 1: Racial Lore*** **PUBLIC**

### Demon

***Overview***  
	The Demon is a result of an Ancient Gargoyle soul, otherwise referred to as an ember, that co-inhabits the body of a host. Many are heavily misunderstood, as their name defines them as dark and dangerous creatures, but often in today’s society, demons can be found living alongside humans, elves, and many other races. Demons are not evil, as many believe them to be. Necromensus, the demon lord, does not oppose the teachings of Aethera, however he believes that power comes from knowledge, not faith.

***Characteristics & Magic***  
	Demons are identified by their host’s racial characteristics, along with a set of horns perched above their head, and a stout gargoyle like tail protruding from behind. Often they have a stone like complexion. Their physical body varies from Demon to Demon, mostly akin to their prior racial background. Demons are usually very intelligent, and have knowledge of many circles of magic, though they see knowledge as the base of magic, and not faith. Many prefer the circle of sorcery, due to its inclination to fire.  
***History***    
Long before the age of mankind, there was another, less human being. Some, in the ways of old, have come to refer to them as gargoyles, the stone monuments carved out to depict these wretched creatures. However, while they lacked in physical beauty, they made great progress in the form of magic. Graced by the goddess Aethera of the light, the gargoyles quickly became masters of fire and earth. But, the great goddess soon became fearful, that the gargoyles would begin to toy with powers that they were unaware of. So, she cast them out, into a new realm of only fire and brimstone. Their bodies burned in the depths of the unlit darkness, but their souls became an unsnuffable ember. After many ages, Aethera once more created beings to wander her world: humans. And, while she may have controlled their knowledge of the magic realm, where there is light, there must also be darkness. Calling from this darkness, a great demon’s voice was heard: Necromensus. He tempted humans with the gifts of fire and earth, that once only the gargoyles knew, but at the price of their mortal body to be shared by the souls of the nether. Aethera grows unpleased by this growing cultist following, however she cannot stop the calling for power. So, she made a deal with the demon lord Necromensus. If he wished to have followers bring back his gargoyles from the beyond, his followers were to remain underground for much of their lives, and cast away their affinity for light.   
A Demon is not born, but is rather created. Demons can be of any race, as long as they are willing to undergo the ritual of the Nether, merging one’s soul with a compatible ember of the nether. These “Embers” are the souls of the gargoyles.

***Culture & Faith***  
Most, if not all demons, live within a society that includes the traditional demon social hierarchy. A demon society, or coven as they are often referred to as, have several key components. Firstly, there is the Patriarch (or Matriarch if female), the political head of the Coven, who does not concern him/herself with the faith and worship of Necromensus. Rather, the leader focuses primarily on the needs of the society, and relations with other factions outside their own. On the other side, there is the faith based sect of the coven, who center themselves around the shrine to the Nether realm. The heads of this sect are called Necromensi, the translators of Necromensus who follow his orders, and conveys them to the Patriarch or Matriarch. Often more times than not, the Necromensi are multiple in number, and spend many hours during their day near the shrine to commune with Necromensus. The Necromensi are chosen among the population for their natural affinity with the nether realm, and their ability to hear the other side better than others. Below the political and faith heads of the coven, there are the Eminent ones, those who have a deep connection to their ember. Many are considered the most powerful among the common Demon, and many have power as generals, and advisors under the hierarchy. Finally, there are the acolytes, and the shriven. A shriven is a person who is not yet demon, but is living among their society. Either they prefer not to receive a demon soul and just wish to be close to Necromensus, or they have yet to undergo the Nether Ritual. After receiving an Ember from the ritual, the shriven becomes an Acolyte, a member of the demon society. Many demon societies are underground, as to keep them closest to their lord, as well as stay in the darkness. While they are not required to live within their own societies, and many do not, demons find it easier to be with others of their same faith, as they cannot reverse the ritual.  
Most demons worship Necromensus, the demon lord, as their god. Necromensus often disputes this claim, as he prefers to be considered just a leader of his people, and the gate-keeper between here and the nether realm, since Gargoyles are unseen. Most covens keep a nether portal open inside their society as a way to communicate directly with Necromensus, and to host rituals within their society instead of demanding a pilgrimage. 

***Naming***  
	Demons have two names: their birth name before the ritual, and their nether name. The latter is a direct merger between the name they were given at birth, and the name of the ember that now resides within them. (Gargoyle names are added after the birth name with a ‘. For example, a human named Jessup Mills, will now be Jess’Hyndra. Gargoyle names are generally more ancient in style.)

***Racial Relations***  
	Most demons are friendly to all races, as their kind does not exclude any race from becoming a demon. After a transformation, some demons even leave a coven and become members of other societies and factions.

***Subtypes***  
	Demons do not per say have specified subtypes, but rather every kind of race appears differently as a demon. The only thing in common between demons is their horns and tail.

### Ent

***Overview***  
	As opposed to common belief, Ents are in fact not sentient beings made from trees. Rather, the walking plant that is the Ent, is really a facade. The real brain is something known as a Heartroot, a parasitic plant growth, much akin to the *album* species. The Heartroot grows deep within a host form, normally humanoid from what it has seen wandering its woods. 

***Characteristics & Magic***  
	Many Ents appear as humanoid beings made out of wood, or some sturdy material with plant life growing from its center. Physically, Ents are strong, but slow, much akin to their perception of time. Mentally, Ents are usually wise beyond their years, as they have seen many a war, and have survived through all of them. However, it is important to note that an Ent does not consider themselves old until they have found their purpose and fulfilled it according to their own personal standards. Many Ents may act young, although they could be ages old, and just have not settled with their standing in the world.   
	While Ents are seen as magical beings due to their sentience, most do not show an affinity towards any specific circle of magic. Ents do seem to show favor towards the circle of clericy, due to the way they grant life to themselves and others, but Ents are not specialists in any form of magic, including clericy.

***History***  
	The origin of the Ent is unknown, as the light goddess Aethera has little knowledge of where they came from. Most speculate the first Ents grew out of the forest, as their species of non sentient *album* is found there. However, there are some Ents that appear like Cacti, and some like seaweed, giving some the speculation that perhaps there are more than one subspecies of Ent. Historically, all though it is outlawed now in many nations, Ents were hunted by Elves for their Heartroot, due to its potent healing properties. This has led to tension between the Ents and Elves for quite some time. 

***Culture & Faith***  
	Ents tend to blend into the culture of where they settle in, as they believe that they must first find their purpose. The only occupation they fear is anything associated with fire. While many Ents are not seen as faithful, and many are in fact nomadic, there is a general faith amongst Ents that praise the Earth Mother, for her life giving gift.   
	Ents see eating as something which is cultural, not persay required. Ents do not have a digestive system, so while they may consume food and chew it, they actually only need water and in most cases, sunlight, to survive.  
	  
***Naming***  
Names of Ents are usually self instituted, and can often change as an Ent goes through its life. The name is usually indicative of the career path the Ent chooses, but again, can change. The naming custom of Ents also is determinate of their age identity. Those that are still wanderers, have the ending \-Sap attached to their name. Those who have settled in their lives have \-Root ending. And finally, those who have retired from their careers and await death, have \-Branch. (An example: Ent who is determined as a farmer, would likely be named Wheat-Root. It is a simple structure.)

***Racial relationships***  
	Ents are usually friendly towards all races, however, there is a deep set fear and hatred of Elves, as the Elves were hunters of Ents in ages before. Also, Ents direct fear of fire has also led to a mostly irrational fear of even the kindest of Demons. 

***Subtypes***  
	Ents have many different forms that have been seen over time, and it is becoming common to name an Ent after the biome in which it seems most affiliated with. Ents cannot become demons.  
Forest Ent: The most basic of Ents, normally made out of wood from an old tree. Also have a tendency to bear fruit.  
Carved Ent: An Ent body that was created from stone or crystal, normally carved by other Ents to harness a Heartroot.  
Desert Ent: An Ent born from a hollow Cactus. The body was meant to survive a long time without much nutrition.  
Mush-Ent: An Ent that grew out of a mushroom, and usually dwells below ground or in heavily shaded regions.  
Sea Ent: An Ent that somehow managed to grow underwater using a mix of coral and seaweed as a body.

### Anthoran

***Overview***  
	The Anthoran are a unique race that some believe originates from the elves. They share many characteristics of animals, as in part, they are animal. All Anthoran have a coming of age ritual that they embark on to find the other half of themselves; their animal spirit. Once found, they merge with it to become one with it, and therefore be considered whole. They are spread out far and wide across the world, and are incorporated deep in the history of many nations.

***Characteristics & Magic***  
	Anthorans have two forms. Their “blank” state, and their “true” form. The blank state is a form before an Anthora has completed their journey, and can be returned to once completed when choosing to walk alongside their animal spirit. Most Anthoran look like a humanoid version of their spirit, and share the same senses their animal spirit does.  
	Anthorans do not seem to show favor towards any form of magic, but some still become mages practicing one or another circle. Like most races, it takes a long time for them to become good at magic, as they do not have a strong sense of magic either. 

***History***  
	The history of the Anthora is checkered at best. Each tribe has legends and myths as to how they came about, but most common Anthorans are spread out in small communities, or other various factions. Most have the belief that they were originally elves that experimented with a circle of nature, but it is unknown if those rumors are true. However, it seems that the traditional coming of age ritual to find one’s spirit animal seems to always be a constant among the history of the Anthoran race.

***Culture & Faith***  
	Most Anthoran culture varies from tribe to tribe, and there is no strong denomination of faith that they tend to favor. Many have specific tribal gods and goddesses, but it rarely spills outside into the more mainstream religions of the world. 

***Naming***  
	Anthoran names take after Elvish origins, suggesting a deeper ancestral tie to the elves. However, in some tribes, Anthorans will have separate names for themselves after their ceremony, leaving their original name to their animal, and naming themselves something entirely different.   
***Racial Relationships***  
	While Anthorans as a people, are considerably well versed with every race, one in particular always seems to derive some level of animosity between them. Nemedi, the mechanical runic race of beings, show a direct disregard for the Anthorans cultures, ways, and mostly everything else, considering it outdated and iconoclast.   
   
***Subtypes***  
	Anthoran subtypes are as diverse as there are animals in the world. Some choose to identify one other form of Anthoran, many refer to as Gillaquids. Gillaquids, are distinctly like Anthorans, and many believe that they are close relatives to the Anthoran race, however, they live primarily below water. Their faith and culture differs much from the Anthoran race as well.

### Gillaquids

	  
***Overview***  
	Anthorans are often the more prominent of the two races, however, Gillaquids are believed to have come from some derivative of the Anthoran bloodline. Gillaquids[^5] are a mostly aquatic race, however, they can spend some time above land before having to return below the water. Many are considered strange by the standards of surface people, thus enforcing the stereotype that Gillaquids prefer to live amongst others of their own kind.

***Characteristics and magic***  
	Gillaquids are not exactly the same as Anthorans, as they are born as they are, and do not have a blank form. Gillaquids resemble many aquatic creatures, ranging from fish, to sharks, to even squids. They often are less nomadic than Anthorans, as they prefer to stay below the water in their communities. Mentally, Gillaquids are normally considered all across the board, ranging from brutish, to gentle and intelligent, but one similarity is their sense of community with one another.   
	Magic is a topic which is all too familiar for Gillaquids, however, their grasp of it is rather limited due to their isolation. Through generations, Gillaquids are taught the basic forms of the water circle of magic, endowing them with the ability to move above water as well, and onto the land. To enhance this further, many Gillaquids have also turned to the progressive forms of technology magic to create suits used to move above water, while keeping in a body environment that is both aquatic and pressurized.

***History***  
	Most prefer to keep the Anthoran and Gillaquid history apart in the books, however, given the elves experimentations with nature circles in the past, it is unclear whether they had a part in the Gillaquid’s creation. Most Gillaquids prefer to remain away from war and the complications of it, and instead have focused almost entirely on their dedication to creation and innovation. As such their history is layered with many inventions throughout the ages, but not much else. Beyond their tendency to be stalwart inventors, not much else is vital about their history, as many say their most recent endeavours above water is truly the start of their history. 

***Culture and Faith***  
	The culture of the Gillaquid is not one of war or exploration, but rather one of invention. While many associate the Nemedi with the innovation and more progressive circles of magic, it is truly the Gillaquids who have been doing it for all of their existence. Within their first five years of life, an Gillaquid is expected to have either invented, or created something worth mention for their family’s namesake. For many ages, it was common for Gillaquids who were not creative or innovative, to be banished from their village until they had a breakthrough of some kind. This was a normal practice up until the last two generations, where Gillaquids have taken an interest in exploring above water with the environment suits designed to keep their body stable on the surface. As such, the practice to invent is slowly becoming more and more obsolete, though some believe the Gillaquids are simply exploring above water to begin a new era of invention with the surface in mind as well.  
	Gillaquids are well aware of the gods and goddesses that inhabit the realms beyond and on the surface, however, as none of them have paid much mind to the race living below the water, Gillaquids are rarely known to worship any god at all. Some do ask for blessings from the progressive gods, but often more times than not, they believe that anything can be achieved without the aid of a deity.

### Nemedi

***Overview***  
	The Nemedi are a fascinating race that continues to gain interest from those who study the ways of the ancient and long forgotten circles of magic. One in particular which has given many researchers a challenge is the circle of tech. While many Nemedi wander the world, few have succeeded in passing their names into history, as many Nemedi were treated as second class citizens up until the current age. 

***Characteristics & Magic***  
	Nemedi appear as an odd assortment of metal objects, leading to many accidentally mistaking them to simply be people in armor. However, under that massive clutter, is nearly nothing except for a singular rune like object, a crystal known to most as a lacrima, or soul gem. Nemedi have been known to change their form on occasion, but most of the time it is a simple adaptation to the gem and it’s growing life. After the lifespan of a Nemedi is completed, the soul inside is released, and awaits a new soul to power it. Often the gem lays dormant for years until it finds a wandering soul to fill it. The magic wipes the memory clean of the soul, and begins a new life, completely clueless, leading to many Nemedi struggling to find their way in life.   
	Nemedi are not normally known to wield magic, however, in a world of people that use magic in daily life, it is hard for them to avoid it completely. Often, Nemedi prefer technology over magic for many scenarios, but this has also lead to a weakening of their lacrima, the very core of their life force. Those that have used magic have noticed one or two years less of their normally one hundred year lifespan. 

***History***  
	The exact origins of the Nemedi race is almost entirely known, however, getting to that point again is nearly impossible. Nemedi were the final creation of the circle of technology, a taboo sect of the magic circles, and now is considered a forbidden magic. The reason so, is because the origins of tech magic began with a combination of psychic, and soul magic, which at the end had deadly results. To create a soul gem, something to possess the body of the Nemedi, required a human sacrifice. Many died in the process of creating these gems, but once they were perfected, many of the original circle mages, sacrificed themselves to gain a new form. They sought immortality, however, upon awaking, they had no memory of their former selves, and have since merged with many other societies for survival.  
	The Nemedi people were noted for their dark origins early on, as many knew of the tragedies that took place in order for the circle to succeed in its measures. Often viewed as the gruesome result, Nemedi were treated as second class citizens up until most recently, where many are given some opportunities afforded to the rest of the races. However, being equal and not feared as some experiment has yet to reach fruition. But, many lucky Nemedi have found themselves adopted into families, as a brother, sister, cousin, or just a friend of the family.   
In recent times, the Nemedi have twisted their magic into a dark arts of tech. They tend to blend in with a highly armored version of a reptile Anthoran with their distinctive black cloak.

***Culture & Faith***  
	Most Nemedi do not have a culture, as it is their nature to be born without a society or family. Those that do make sure to pass away with people who will welcome the new soul as almost a child of the former. Nemedi have on occasion been known to worship Necromensus, the demon lord, as often they deem him as a lord of knowledge. While they themselves cannot become a demon, and host an ember, many times they are greeted amongst demon societies with honor, as many demons also face the cruel reality that their appearances and origins can scare the commoner. 

***Naming***  
	Nemedi are often poor when it comes to naming themselves, and usually end up with the strangest of names. Many have noticed Nemedi names are directly related to the first thing they see, and can identify. However, those who don’t name themselves, and instead awake to find themselves with family around them, will often take the name granted to them. (In this case, a common name for a Nemedi could be Nail, or even Rock.) 

***Racial Relationships***  
	Nemedi do not hate any race in particular, but have deep angst against the many races that viewed them as monsters. While most hear the stories and legends of the circle of tech and their cruelties, they are only hurt when others enact that fear and hatred back to them. The only race they seem to have no fear of, and actually tend to be most often associated with, are Demons.

 ***Subtypes***  
	There is no direct subtypes of the Nemedi, but rather their materials are what diversify them. Nemedi also have a tendency to take form of whatever soul inhabits them at the given time, but that is not to say that a Nemedi who grows close to a specific race will not begin to form attributes of such race. (You can have a Nemedi that looks like an Ent, Anthoran, or even Demon).They are not genderless however, and usually identify one way or the other. 

### Formori

***Overview***  
	The Formori is a fairly new creation, as their origin was to fight for the Wars of the Third age. Some consider them the more organic alternative to the original focus of the Nemedi’s creation, however, most Formoris are hostile to many outside their own race, but they dominate the great arenas that litter the world.

***Characteristics & Magic***  
	Formoris are a physically powerful race. Their bodies are born from the earth itself, giving them a hard shell, or exoskeleton in which many use as their armor. While most cannot see under their solid rock exoskeleton, under it is believed to be a soft mass of muscle, much akin to insects whom they are most related to. The Formori race have not two, but four eyes, two in front, and two on their sides, in which was specifically formed for combat. Mentally, Formoris strive for combat, making many spectators and competitors in the arena. They are in fact not the smartest of any race, and often are regarded as the dumbest, but their battle strategy skills have far surpassed their Elvish creators.  
	After a Formori dies in battle, their new body is grown from the water. Formoris, as their original purpose was for war, their bodies mature quickly, moving from birth to adolescence to adulthood within mere weeks. In adulthood they stop aging, as it seems only death can be their end. However, after death, they are quickly reincarnated anew, from the blessed waters. But, unknown to the elves, as their water spread through the rivers, Formoris can seemingly be born from anywhere alongside a waterbed.   
	Magic is often regarded as a taboo of the Formoris, but some have been known to wield it or study it time to time. Formoris normally rely on their extremely strong bodies to fight in hand to hand, or weapon based combat, and have rarely been seen with any weapon of range. 

***History***  
	The Formori are one of the three created races, Nemedi and Demons often considered close relatives by the non created races. Formoris were created for use by the Elves during the Third Era Wars, to make up for the Elves deficiencies in combat. After the wars, Glyhics, though regarded by Elves as simply tools for a war, were indeed sentient, and were cast away from the Elvish homeland in the Kingdom of Wood for their warlike personalities that conflicted with the Elvish ways. The Banishment has created a heavy rift between the Formori and their creators, but since then, most Formori have settled down in Elvish like Tribal communities, primarily populated by the Formori. Others have moved into large cities which have arenas in which they can compete for glory and fame, or to live as a guard, always prepared to fight for justice.  
Their creation came from the ancient circle of divinity, a pure form of magic directly related to the way the gods originally created life. The elvish elders blessed the Origin Spring, a massive lake that sits in the Kingdom of Wood, and has many rivers running from it, some even into the ocean.

***Culture & Faith***  
	The culture of the Formori people is riddled with stories of war and glorious battles. It is common for a young Formori to be adventurous, as it is encouraged by their elders for all to seek their fame. While some of their culture and social structure comes from the elves, they incorporate their lust for battle as part of their society. The elders, as they are often referred to, are not exactly the oldest, but rather the most powerful. Every year, a new group of elders is selected from the trials, a series of battles between the strongest individuals in the tribe for who will be leader. The results of the trials are a direct correlation to the positions the elders have, as seniority plays no role either.   
	Formori families are somewhat similar to the Nemedi, having roots near wherever they are born. However, most tribes have taken advantage of the benefits of the water rebirth, and formed their communities near certain spawning spots. Also, because of this, a tradition is held every year that the Formori rebinds him or herself to the blessing of the water, and therefore ensuring that upon death, they will return with their memories and amongst their relatives and friends once more. It is not uncommon for children in a family to end up raising their parents until they are of age as well.  
	As death is not a subject of fear amongst the Formori, many lead reckless lives in search of their glory and honor. Formori are usually regarded as some of the most courageous of the races, and will take up nearly any job that toys with death. However, as death is a subject of direct rebirth, and their memories remain in tact over every lifetime, Formoris who hope to start anew do not renew their blessing. Without the blessing, the Formori is born without their memories, and normally far from their tribe’s water source, usually closest to where they die.   
	While originally some older Formori believe that their one true goddess is Nemistri, the creator of the Wood, many of the new generation believe that their goddess has forsaken them, just as the elves did. Instead, they have begun to worship Zweihanar the god of war who guided their hands in battle and after, it was he who lead the Formori people from the Wood. Often referred to as First Ancestor, Zweihanar is an honorary Formori, and as legends hold, his glorious feats will be passed into all of the Formori people, as long as they hold fast to the beliefs of Zweihanar: glory and honor is obtained through battle.

***Naming***  
	The names of the Formori are often one in the same with their past life, making many names consistent throughout the ages. More often than not, since the Formori are born akin to the age of five in human years, they can speak and thus name themselves. Even a Formori who has lost their memories, will often remember their name. (Formoris, if you don’t know by now, are basically orcs with 4 eyes. Thus, name it like an orc).

***Racial Relationships***  
	The Formori have a strange way of communicating, as often most others perceive as aggression, is really just how they treat everyone. Because of that, they tend not to make friends with any races in particular. On the other side, the Formori have a certain disdain for two races: Nemedi, and the elves. Nemedi is likely because the Formori are normally compared to them on a regular basis, and elves because of their checkered past after the third era wars. 

 ***Subtypes***  
	The Formori have no specific subtypes, and are in fact one of two races (the other is Nemedi), who cannot become a demon. Each Formori comes in a variety of shapes and sizes, and they identify as either male or female. 

### Endaurs

***Overview***  
	The mysterious race of beings that wander out from the end. Pilgrims from a broken world, hoping to start anew in a great world. But, is their intentions pure, or shall they bring the same destruction upon their new world, as it is believed that they brought upon in their old one.   
***Characteristics & Magic***  
	The Endaur race is a humanoid race of beings, that nearly looks identical to elves, however, their almost void black skin and purple eyes set them apart. Their physical strength is actually quite lacking, as many are considered to be weak in strength, however, what they lack, they make up for in immense knowledge. As such, many Endaurs are esteemed mages, perhaps even more so than Elves, but that is up to debate. They seem to have a stronger affinity to dark magic, thus birthing the term “Dark Elf” to classify their species.  
***History***  
	Endaurs came from beyond the void. Before their exodus from the End, as it has become commonly referred to, not much is known about the Endaurs. Endaurians distinctly don’t write down their history, and instead it is passed down through generations by their ancestors. As such, their history only depicts two great events in the other realm. One, was the birth of the dragon. It has plagued the world of the End for as long as their people have known, and travellers to the abandoned realm consider it a worthy challenge to attempt at finally slaying the beast for good. But, it is to no avail, as every time, the dragon is reborn. The other event was the great plague. Some consider it a combination of insanity, and a physical warping of the body. Whatever the plague is, it contorts the victim into strange slim and tall creatures. While they resemble the Endaurs, these Endermen, as they have been come to be called, are a threat to all who encounter them. Endermen, the afflicted of the end plague, have a drive to snatch precious resources from the world, and return them to their homeland, for what some believe is their attempt at rebuilding the broken world. The Endaurs brought the Endermen with them from the void, but quickly made note that they would take care to ensure they would not become a nuisance upon the world. While many view their promises as empty, it is vastly difficult for Endaurs to kill others whom once may have been a friend or a relative.   
***Culture & Faith***  
	Endaurs have their own system of society, often using a chamber of intellectuals to guide their ways. Many decisions made by the intellectuals affect entire communities of Endaurs and their surrounding villages as well. While they might not be entirely spiritual, it seems that Endaurs split their culture between magic, and faith. Magic, to the common dark elf, should be considered a great honor to wield, and therefore many dark elves practice it only when necessary, or when in study. But, they make sure to keep it separated from their faith.  
	The Endaur faith revolves around two gods, the twins. One, is the goddess of the past, Alpea, and the other is the god of the future, Omgion. Dark elves pray to both in different respects, the past to grant them wisdom of their history, and give them knowledge from ages long ago, and the future to guide their way and hopefully keep them safe in their travels into the unknown future.  
***Naming***  
	The Endaurs are also considered elves, as their naming system reflects rather closely to the elves’ style, but lack some fluency in the style too. Where there is often an “S”, the Endaur language uses a V instead, since there is a lack of the “S” sound. Also, the ‘Th” sound is not something within their language, so instead a “Z” replaces it. (So for a name like Serenith, it would be Vereniz instead).  
***Racial Relationships***  
	Endaurs are not a hostile race, otherwise they would have died out long ago. They are actually considered among some of the top political powers amongst the races, and many Endaurs have taken seats of power to ensure equality for their pilgrim brothers and sisters. In fact, most are rather well spoken and as such, have managed to form solid relationships with many of the races.  
 ***Subtypes***  
	There are no direct subtypes of Endaurs, but they are one of the races that can become demons, although most Endaurs would consider this a direct casting out of their faith. 

### Goblins

Goblins are not a playable race yet.  They are, however a race that is throughout Deluvia and able to be interacted with.

## *Section 2: Religious Lore* PUBLIC

**Religious Lore:**

Within the first era of Deluvia, there were those that killed the ancient dragons to ascend beyond their own souls. These beings created were created through the fallen scales of ancient dragons, but killed their creators to surpass them into legend, and the great Aetheric and Endaric realms beyond. These beings, gods as they are often referred to, now dictate the worlds workings from their new home, the land of immortality, however, some have returned to ensure their worship from the beings that still inhabit Deluvia. Though, some believe their return has harrowed the great deluge, as the angered dragons who now exist as one with the world, rupture and split the land to destroy all that the gods care for. 

Gods exist in many realms, in which have often determined who has worshiped them over the ages.  
**Aetheric:** The realm beyond, where the gods who orient themselves with faith are often from. It is considered to be an immortal realm somewhere locked out of time, but is normally pictured as a place of light and perfection.

**Endaric:** The void realm, a place of darkness and mystery, often associated with gods of knowledge and progress. As an alternative to ascencion, some gods proceeded into the end to study the unknown land. 

**Deluvic:** The realm of the surface. Dominated by the mortal races, and once by the gargoyles, gods, and dragons before them. Deluvic gods are those that have returned to their land of origin to bestow knowledge, or ensure faith, amongst the mortal races.

**Netheric:** The final realm of fire and brimstone that had existed once as perhaps the home to the ancient dragons, now used as a prison for the souls of the gargoyles. A realm dominated by one god, or lord as he is often referred to, Necromensus, and, is home to his wife, Embreas. 

***Faith Gods:*** Often regarded as the first gods, these are the most prominent of the gods who have many who know, and worship them. Their primary goddess is Aethera.

**Aetheric**\- Aethera, the goddess of light and worship. Aethera is often regarded as the mother of all the gods, and perhaps the most powerful. She was the first to ascend, and is normally associated with light and worship. She has taken a backseat to current worshiping practices, and is rarely heard from, even by those who are her most diligent priests. She is said to have dictated the roles of the other ascended, and their powers. Aethera is normally depicted as a being of light, without a physical body.

**Deluvic**\- Zweihanar, the god of war. Zweihanar is the honorary First Ancestor of the Formori people as he was their guide out of the Wood. He is often considered taboo to worship, as he takes a position on the battlefield alongside whichever side pleases him most on a whim. His powers are guaranteed victory to those whom he sides with, though he has been known to switch sides. He has appeared in many time periods, however, one thing in common is he prefers to hide his true form in a massive dark suit of armor, thorned and bloody from many battles. It is feared that one day he shall rise alone and proceed to wage war against all mortals for his own humor.

**Endaric**\- Tresola, the goddess of chaos and luck. Tresola is often one of the least common gods to worship. However, though she might not be a primary goddess with many followers, she does get a fair share of worship from those who wish for luck, and possibly for bad luck to fall upon others. She resides in the Endaric realm, though often appears in Deluvia using her shapeshifting powers to deceive others for the sake of chaos. Her true form depicted in art is usually a mixture of many creatures, thus further depicting her chaotic nature. Tresola is the sole inhabitant of a sub-Endaric realm, originally intended as a prison for her, designed by the gods in the Aetheric realm to control her chaos. However, with her deceptive skills, Tresola managed to gin control of the realm, and in turn, anchored it to the Deluvic realm for all existence. Her very presence in Deluvia is often attributed for all manners of misfortune, and great fortune alike. Recently, in order to attain a greater standing of power, she has opened her gates to the mortal world, allowing Deluvians to pass into dungeons of chaos she creates to entertain herself with. Those that succeed can be guaranteed great fortune, but those that fail can be assured death. 

***Traditional Gods:*** Gods that tend to be worshiped among the common people. Normally do not ally themselves in the battle between faith and knowledge, but still embody a large force of god-like power. Their primary god is Sifaneus.

**Aetheric**\- Finora, goddess of natural forces. Finora is the very embodiment of the natural realm and all it’s elements. She is normally regarded as the elemental goddess, however, she takes a very lite role in the circles of magic. Although Finora remains in the Aetheric realm, she is not as dominant of a primary goddess, as Sifaneus is the more notable of the traditional gods. Finora is depicted as a being of earth, water, and air, caring for the world, over it’s inhabitants. As such, she also is considered a goddess of life and death, and is prayed to by those who wish to prolong their life in times of illness. 

**Deluvic**\- Sifaneus, God of Justice and leadership. The most prominent of the Traditional gods, and perhaps one of the strongest forces of all the gods in Deluvia. He actively sits as a king among the mortals, as both judge and jury of the people. While he is normally regarded as a fair and equal king, some grow weary of the leadership of an unaging god, and in the past have challenged his regime, to their own demise. He is often depicted in his royal attire and seated on his massive throne. 

**Netheric**\- Embreas, goddess of the hearth and family. Embreas is a rare example of a rogue goddess. Her sorrowful history began when she descended during the second era, for her love of the Gargoyles. Her compassion for all living beings lead her to fall in love with Necromensus, one who pursued knowledge for the betterment of all. But, their forbidden love is often regarded as the downfall of the gargoyle race, along with his relentless pursuit of knowledge, and possibly ascension. After his kind was banished from the world, she joined him in the Netheric realm, not as a lover, but as an eternal wife. Her compassion and love are regarded as reason to worship her, as she has become the symbol of the hearth in every home. Families believe the hearth will bring her warmth into their home and hearts. 

***Progressive Gods:*** Less like gods, and more like great teachers. The progressive gods take a very active role in the wisdom and knowledge of magic, and often will make great impacts in history throughout the ages. The most prominent of the progressive gods is Necromensus, however, he is also the least powerful. 

**Netheric**\- Necromensus, the Demon lord of the Nether and seeker of knowledge. Before he was cast from the world, he was an esteemed master of many circles of magic. His prowess however, was deemed the curse of his race, the ancient gargoyles. Aethera and the other gods feared his power, and cast him to the nether, where he takes a rather active role as a purveyor of research of knowledge and magic through his demon followers. He is the gatekeeper of the Netheric realm, assisting in the transfer of embers into their hosts without fail. 

**Deluvic**\- Astorius, the god of the cosmos. Astorius was one of two gods who sided with Necromensus in his plight for knowledge. Astorius is wise beyond many, knowledgeable in the great circle of cosmic magic, and takes an active role with his followers in the citadel known as the observatory. While many of his practice have disappeared over the years, legend has it that he still sits in the decaying observatory with his remaining followers, peering into the great beyond, trying to decipher celestial runes and call upon the powers. However, there are those that believe his perception of the great beyond can be used to dominate the land.

**Endaric**\- Aplea and Omgion, the twins of past and future. The twins of the Dark Elf race only began to be worshiped within the late third era, as they represented two gods who came over from the void realm of the end. Alpea and Omgion were the first to teach the Endaurians how to travel through portals into Deluvia, however, some believe they were also responsible for assisting Necromensus in communicating through the nether portal to his first followers. They are not actively involved in the politics of the world, but instead are worshiped for their powers of vision of past and future. Alpea, goddess of the past, is a connection to ancestral spirits who have passed into the void. Omgion is the guide of the future, worship for his riddles that predict events to come. They are normally depicted as dark elves, though one with white eyes, and the other with dark eyes. 

***Other Gods:*** So, terms do not exactly fit those who’ve managed to ascend beyond mortal status, as these beings have not persay been accepted by the first and second era gods. These, “other” gods, tend to find themselves in a classification limbo, as usually, they do not fit in among the common religious practices, and nor do they have many worshipers who grant them a title of a diety worth worship. That being said, it is possible to ascend to the status of a god, though the method is normally involving a deal with an already existing god, and usually will require a matter of eternal servitude as their minor. Thus, normally only the relatively insane, or those with nothing better to do, will go after the challenges put forward by the gods in order to become one. 

**Deluvic**\- Anona, the Chronicler. Like most Deluvic gods, Anona walks among mortal kind. Unlike most Deluvic gods, Anona does not see fit to be called a god in any way or form, and thus has a tendency to hide their god-hood from others. That being said, Anona became a god through the challenge of Astorius, as they were given the task to chronicle all the happenings, in all the world, at the same time. An impossible task for a human, but Anona in turn asked to be granted a deity like power to walk among the mortals for eternity, appear in multiple places at once, and be guised as anything, or anyone in order to complete such a massive task. Wise as he was, Astorius granted the wish unknowingly, giving Anona the status of a god, who now simply wanders our world. As such, Anona can be anyone or anything, always watching, and recording. His or her (they come in many forms) words can be found in almost every history book, and even in many newspapers, often making others assume mortal authors use the name as well, to gain fame for their publishings. 

***Main quest: Forbidden Rising***

In the main quest-line, the player discovers that there is a rising power called the Forbidden Truth trying to ascend their leader to become a god, through dubious sacrifices. The main quest-giver will provide the player with a pretty straightforward goal, but with multiple possibilities. 

Beginning: The Origins of War

“In the North, there is a group growing in power. They call themselves the Forbidden Truth. Apparently they want to become gods or something. I don’t really know all the details, but hey, if you want to figure it out, go ahead.”

Decision: Divided 3 ways, go to the capital of each kingdom and find an attendant of the court to give you more information on how bad the Forbidden Truth is, and how they’re trying to stop it, so you have to join them, blah blah blah.

OR: Travel north and come across one of their sacrificial temples, and get inducted as a member by killing an NPC.

Key decision: To Kill a God

This one is a bit trickier, as it has 4 different possibilities. 3 depending on your kingdom, and 1 if you’re part of the cult. 

Decision: Once more, 3 ways depending on your kingdom. It works sort of like rock paper scissors, as each kingdom has one that they are hunting, and one that they are hunted by. For example, Faith attacks Progress, Progress attacks Tradition, and Tradition attacks Faith. I’ll flesh out the reasoning for each later, especially when we write out NPC quest dialogue. The Gods that are being hunted are the Deluvic ones listed above. Depending on Kingdom alliance, you will hunt one god for a piece of their soul to return them to their realm of origin (Endaric or Aetheric) so they can no longer exist in Deluvia. I think upon reaching the god, there will be two options available to the player. One, will be simply to fight the god a PNPC that will result in the drop of the soul shard (a renamed end crystal). The other option is to do it completely in roleplay, essentially trying to convince the god to hand over their shard as the player is considered worthy. I see this going three ways depending on the boss. Progress (God of knowledge) requires a hefty Intelligence stat, Traditional (God of Leadership) requires a strong Charisma stat, and Faith (God of War) requires a strong Strength stat. 

OR: As this is a much less desirable path by players, the difficulty and yield will be much higher. Every player in this path has to defeat not one, but all three of the gods, retrieving their shards to sacrifice to the cult leader for ascension. 

Final section: Ending Ascension / Gods Among Us

This is the final result of the questline, and a turning point for the history of the game. It is actually a large server event, held for multiple weeks during probably a month or so, and it is basically a massive PVP event. After the decisions of the prior quests, the players will be tasked to defeat or defend the cult leader during his ascension ceremony. Now, here’s where it gets interesting. The Cult Leader boss (PNPC) will be given extra armor, health, and even weapons, based on how many shards were retrieved by players allied in his quest line. The fights will take place in the weeks before his ascension, as the kingdoms are trying to weaken him before he has a chance to ascend. The battles will be between 1-8 player teams from the kingdoms, versus 1-4 player teams from the cult \+ the cult leader boss. Now, the kingdom teams also have a benefit on their side. Depending on which god was killed the most, the players from every kingdom will receive a special weapon that emphasizes that god’s powers. 

Results: Should the Kingdoms succeed and weaken the boss enough to a point where he cannot ascend, they shall be victorious, and the players will get an extra reward from their kingdom of choice, along with the rewards gained if they or their party defeat the cult leader.

OR: Should the Kingdoms fail, the Cult leader shall ascend to god status, and enter the Aetheric realm. As a reward for their compliance, he gives his followers an extra reward on top of what they gained if they or their party defeated the onslaught party. 

Lore changes: This is a big one. As this concludes chapter one of the server, we will add in the results of player decisions into the lore. 

The Kingdoms- The Kingdom that had the most success (quest completion) will be deemed the most powerful of the period, and the other two shall also be labeled in kind. 

The Gods- The god that was killed the most will now be considered bound to his prior realm. He will no longer exist in Deluvia, essentially leaving a void for the Kingdom that benefitted from that god the most.

The Cult- This one hinges entirely on the results of the event. Should the Kingdoms succeed and trump the cult leader, the cult will become less influential, and the leader will eventually begin looking into other methods to ascend, leading to the decline of the cult following through the years. The more interesting scenario is if the cult succeeds and he ascends. If he manages to ascend, he will take his place as the new god of the occult, embodying all that is involved with sacrifice and blood magic. He is considered the god of contracts, and will become perhaps something for a later quest-line. 

**Class progression**

Fighter+ Rogue \= Weapon Master

Fighter+ Mage \= Runic blade

Fighter+ Cleric \= Paladin

Fighter+ wanderer \= Mercenary

Rogue \+ Mage \= Thief

Rogue \+ Cleric \= Monk

Rogue \+ Wanderer \= Explorer

Mage \+ Cleric \= Elemental

Mage \+ Wanderer \= Spellsword

Cleric \+ Wanderer \= Troubadour

Ranger \+ Mage \= Shaman

Ranger \+ Fighter=  Hunter

Ranger \+ Rogue \= Assassin 

Ranger \+ Cleric \= Druid

Ranger \+ Wanderer \= Scout

Ranger x2 \= Beast Master

Fighter x2 \= Guardian

Rogue x2 \= Ninja

Mage x2 \= Sorcerer

Cleric x2 \= Disciple

Wanderer x2 \= Boundless.

**Section Six: Covenants**

The Macabre vineyards. 

A company widely known around Deluvia for their wines and spirits. However, deep beneath their professional exterior, lies a secret society dedicated to the company and their secrets. The Vineyard's leaves, as they are known, are assassins, known to attack seemingly at random, simply to kill those who have been tagged by the company for reasons unknown to the public. Rumors say that they chose their victims according to their blood type, or rarity, as radicals believe the Vineyard mixes the blood in to make it taste even rarer, or even darker, as a sort of ritual for the goddess Tresola, to bring fortune to their family and company. You clearly have your reasons for being a Leaf of the Vinyard, 

May your chalice always be full.

The Iron Chapel.

Becoming a member of the Iron Chapel requires great experience and even greater valor. There are two ways members have been known to join. One, is finding the first chapel, an ancient arena once used to house the Chapel's battles, now a well sought after secret. Finding it permits an initiation by combat, and winning grants membership to the Chapel. The second, is through notoriety, be it through heroism, or injustice, should one be a force to be feared, they can be brought in for the same trial should the challenge be accepted. Once accepted, members of the Chapel, otherwise known as Combatants, are pitted against one another in combat. The winner continues in the favor of the covenant, and in the favor of Zweihanar the God of war, while the loser will be lowered in their ranks. 

Your battles will bring you glory, and failures shall be met with new insights\!

Finora's Morticians

Life and death are a sacred order. The goddess of nature ensures this as best she can, but her sacred oath must be enforced. So, there are those who dig the graves, the graves of ones who wish to bring death prematurely to others. These are her Morticians, the grave diggers and keepers of Finora's order. They are staunchly opposed to the Vinyard, the ones who seek out death in order to please their goddess of luck. All they see is chaos and misfortune, so, to save this world, it is their duty to preserve life, by ending the lives of those who disrupt it. 

Your goddess calls, and the graves must be dug.

The Third King's Bards

Ages prior, there was a king who needed to redeem the legacy of his reign. As such, he sought out the bards from around the world, those who would follow both heroes, and villains alike, and revel the tales of their exploits. He summoned them to his chamber to reveal to him these stories. Many believe this are the first chroniclers, the followers of the God Anona, the wanderer. However, long past his death, the bards continued into legend, their order still following and aiding, and returning to the grave of the old king to tell him these legends, and receive in turn his gifts. 

Rally on and seek legends of glory\!

Shades of the Crypt

The shadows have always been feared throughout history, until the age of light whence it banished darkness for some time. As fire grows, and houses stay lit, the shadows must creep in the underground, and in the streets. But, there are those who seek this darkness, pining after the one truth they believe lies in the unknown. The banished God Crypto, lord of Shadows, his life in the deep Endaric realm, and his knowledge of the Netharic. A taboo Union of darkness and void, and yet, seek it they do, to become his servants. The Shades are those who hide themselves in the darkness, and flee from the light, as their power and knowledge only grows whence light is no more. 

Go now, expand the shadows to honor your God.

God Crypto: Origin-Endaric. Crypto was once a minor God hidden away in the realms of the Endaric, often forgotten. His knowledge has spanned millenniums in the Deluvic realm, yet only so much can be learnt from observing mortals in their realm. He left, though, for many who leave it is to Deluvia to study closer, or for worship. But, he dove deeper, to the realm of fire and brimstone. Few know what he was seeking, or if he found it, but now he resides in his sub-realm, tucked away from sight. The Crypt of Shadows, a dark and forbidden place. A burial ground for those who wish to serve him in this life and the next as his ever expanding shadow. A library of forbidden knowledge of the End and Nether, yet to see it with eyes that are still pure, would be to have one's soul reduced to nothing more than a shadow of their former self. And yet, those that seek it, can pursue this knowledge. Their faith to him is boundless, and in return he grants them the concord of shadows, a pact to use his powers to shroud themselves. He is often not known to other gods, but in Deluvia, he and his Shades are a legend of fear often told to children at night. But, where there is legend, there is often truth behind it.

Function of covenants. Covenants are server owned non player factions that can be joined by finding them or by completing certain prerequisites. They are optional and do not hamper or assist the player in the progression of major quest lines.

Plugin: the plugin for covenants will be rather extensive, requiring Minecraft to read certain items and add extra functions to the player when equipped in a special inventory slot.

Covenant item functions: the function of the covenant items is to provide the player with access to new options that were not allowed before. These items cannot be lost, and if they are accidentally discarded, they can be obtained through a /kit command that is unlocked when the player first joins the covenant. 

Current covenants, covenant items, and new access to player: 

vineyard:

New title(s)- Withered Leaf; White Leaf; Red Leaf.

New Commands- /warp Vineyard /invade /accept /deny

Command functions- /warp vineyard allows players to warp directly to the covenant location. /invade allows players to invade other players (including fellow covenant members) who are in danger zones (pvp enabled locations). /accept allows players to invade to assist other members of their covenant in pvp if a Mortician has been added in combat against them. /deny allows players to not invade and thus not assist the fellow covenant member.

New function in chat- Other covenant members are highlighted in green; "Leaves blow in the wind, do you accept the call?" Message in chat, prompting players to the /accept or /deny commands.

Rewards- Upon killing enemies when invading, receive Blood leaves, to be returned to the covenant. A stack of 10 earns the White Leaf title. A stack of 20 earns the Red Leaf title. A stack of 30 earns the Leaf Assassin class and the weapon Leaf Blade.

Morticians:

New Title(s)- Grave Digger, Embalmer, Mortician.

New Commands- /warp Finoras graveyard /accept /deny

Command Functions- /warp Finoras graveyard allows players to warp directly to the covenant location. /accept allows players to join a player who has been invaded to combat the invader. /deny rejects the prompt to teleport.

New Functions in chat- "Your goddess calls, and the graves must be dug." A message prompt to allow players access to the commands /accept or /deny to attack an invader. 

Rewards- Upon killing an enemy invader, gain Transgressor Ashes to be returned to the covenant. A stack of 10 earns the title Embalmer. A stack of 20 earns the title Mortician. A stack of 30 earns the class Virtuous Acolyte, and the weapon Last Rites.

Chapel:

 New title(s)- Combatant, Inducted, Veteran

New Commands- /warp Chapel

Command Functions- /warp chapel allows covenant members to teleport to the chapel arena for combat.

New Functions in Chat- N/A

Rewards- Upon killing an opponent in the arena gains Broken Bone. A stack of 10 earns the title Inducted. A stack of 20 earns the title Veteran. A stack of 30 earns the class IronBorne, and the weapon Bloodrust. 

Bards:

 New title(s)- Literate, Studious, Chronicler

New Commands- /warp Third kings chamber /accept /deny

Command Functions- /warp third kings chamber allows players to warp directly to the covenant location. /accept allows players to accept the request of another player to assist in a dungeon. /deny counters the request to teleport.

New Functions in Chat- "A bard's company has been requested." A message appearing to covenant members to join other players who request support in a dungeon, allowing response via /accept or /deny to teleport to the player in need. "A bard has joined your company." A message appearing to the player who requested assistance when a bard accepts the request to teleport.

Rewards- Upon killing an opponent in the arena gains Tale of Valor. A stack of 10 earns the title Studious. A stack of 20 earns the title Chronicler. A stack of 30 earns the class Anona, and the weapon Nameless Dialect. 

Shades:

 New title(s)- Lurker, Malign, Nightmare

New Commands- /warp Crypt 

Command Functions- /warp crypt allows covenant members to teleport to the covenant area.

New Functions in Chat- N/A

Rewards- Upon completing the first series of quests gain the title Malign. Upon completing the second series of quests gain the title Nightmare. Upon completing the final series of quests, gain the class Void Shade, and the weapon Chasm's Edge.

# Deluvic: Language of the First Mortals

Drasil: Magic wood  
Urd: Ruler  
Nyan: Gift  
Mynith: moon  
Darg: dark  
Broth: breath

Other languages are Aetheric, the language of the Gods and Endauric the language of the void

# **Dungeons of Deluvia**

Note to staff:  
Quests and dungeons should always contain 

1. combat component  
2. narrative component  
3. puzzle component  
4. reward component. 

   Each room of a dungeon, for example, can reinforce and contribute to these 4 components.

   

   Dungeons are a type of quest and playable area, that and again is just a useful word to describe an area to be solved. The word dungeon, in-game, should be used as a jail in a castle.

   

   Dungeons are solvable puzzles, usually with a boss or mini-boss that a group of players, or a player by themselves, can traverse to find an end result and get  treasure and skills. They are places that have secret passages, kill unique skilled NPCs, and retrieve rare artifacts. Dungeons may be be permeable and in context with other non-dungeon areas, such as the sewer below New Pallamost but they may also follow the rules of seamless everworld, where they are whole new playable areas. 

   Dungeons can also be assigned a Level in our documentation (but not in game), to describe the difficulty and the loot table to be assigned with it. 

   Dungeons may be a step in a larger quest, or be stand-alone. They may be themed as part of a quest, or themed with some other metanarrative. 

The 12 Cursed Palaces  of Deluvia  
Though there are many questable adventure areas in Deluvia, these are the 12 major/large themed dungeons.  
At the time the 12 Sages were sprung out of the Omphalos, the darker forces of Deluvia created 12 majora demonus of the 12 Demon clans.
