## The Stone Temple of Tantalon Remis Mines

*Tanta*, in the old Deluvic means Despise and *Remis* means, the first or initial, and this temple was dedicated to the demise and despisement of the mortal race. It is located in the Riftlands (-20, 256, 2847\) among the rifts and was the god’s, that hated the mortals, answer to the Omphalos. Where the Omphalos is where the mortals sprung up, this pit is where the mortals are dragged down.

Early on Hythlodaeus,, the god of fire and chaos, kennelled his mega beast, **Zalrumurlith the abominate** in this pit. Zalrumurlith would wait on the bottom of this pit that resembled a mine to entice the mortals down into it with desire for rare ores.

### Zalrumurlith The Abominate and The Pit Keepers

	Zalrumith is a beast born of the flame of Hythloadaeus, and the metals of earth were split into many by the effects of his birth. Him being made of solely fire and metal made him melt and reform into several of himself. All of the same soul but different amounts of material. They all are connected, once one feels another perish they receive a signal and begin to challenge the one who has defeated him to fight the next. He detests those who don’t accept his challenge. For they are the foolish who challenged him in his weaker forms.  
	Zalrumith is made of several types of elements, each being stronger the deeper travel happens. For they wish to go down to the core of the elements. The core of the world. But for his weaker counterparts to get that far they need more metal. Therefore he resides in the pit. Collecting ores and killing those who he will take elements from.  
	Once he grows strong enough and combines all himself to one, it’s said he will leave the cavern and challenge all those who are not metal or flame. For he despises them. For they are the ones who casted him into the pit were not made of such material of his own. 

The players begin at the top of the mine pit  in the Riftlands. They have to make their down the slopes. They may meet some stone elementals and stone phantoms swooping at them on their way down. Once they reach the bottom, they jump into their descent.

Layers  
	Each layer has its own set of ores and items. As well as mobs\!   
Layer 1  
Layer 1 will have several monsters made of stone and little reward. As they go down layers they will receive messages about the heat level increasing. Giving mining fatigue, slowness, and eventually blindness.  
	The first gate will be accessible to all. The boss Zalrumith must be defeated in his first form in order to be challenged by its next on the second layer back in the pit. Which the players must backtrack to.   
Layer 2  
	The second layer will have several fire monsters which will cause fire damage and have little defence from players attacks. They will drop blacksmithing tomes and lava crystals. Once more Zalrumith must be slain to receieve the challenge from the next level.

Synonyms to *Despise* for use in items and other theme: execrate, detest, hatred, disdain, disfavor, deplore, discountenance, loathe

## Jutrollag Basilica

Jutrollag Basilica was once the Palace Chor Bematic Riftenbleak by the Old Gods. Shortened to Riftenbleak. Charltrolate the devourer was an ancient and deep beast living in the caverns beneath Riftenbleak. When the goddess Expitik fled the core lands and arrived out here Charltrolate thought she would be a tasty treat, for he enjoyed devouring demigods like this. But for some reason he had sympathy for Expitik and her turmoils in the core lands, as the ancient beasts and titans had no love lost for the Central Kingdoms. Charltrolate and Expitik struck a deal that he take his upcoming dormancy period to lay low under the basilica while the Jutrollag people came. Expitik agreed to keep the mortals power limited and the town a small one. Charltrolate, as powerful as he was, knew that mortals would eventually, in a century or so, overcome the beasts of the deep so he tried to play his cards right. He outlived the gods, and he so shall outlive the mortals.. This name stuck because he also is able to devour souls through his minions called devourers, for which he saps some of their soul for energy and gains insight into their fears.

When Expitik left Riftenbleak go, Charltrolate came out of his dormancy very hungry. His many minions overran the old Jutrollag Basilica and returned the Riftenbleak Palace in the ruins.

Now known to the mortals as “Cowardice” because this space is intended to reduce warriors to cowards, one of Charltrolate pet goals. Charltrolate has a special grudge against the god Zweihanar, the god of war, because he feels the gods and mortals valor is an artiface that could crumble under the titans and beasts of old. Though Charltrolate knows he is not powerful enough to eat Zweihanar yet, he is biding his time to take feast on each god all the way to the most powerful. Each adventurer that comes into his lair is merely practice.

Kalimvane was the first settlement of the Jutrollag pilgrims who set up the big basilica in honor of their god **Expitik**. Expitik has long gone from the basilica and all that are left are monsters. 

BACKSTORY: Expitik is a good goddess and was outcast from Druvenrog when they turned their backs on gods and magic long ago.   
The **Jutrollag Union Brotherhood** was an old and respected guild at Druvenrog. **Terriss** was the lead cleric and **Uftan** was his cupholder. This was at a time when there were many guilds on Druvenrog and many had their own religions.   
Druvenrog started to dive deeper into technology after the Wars of the Third Age. Any type of arcane thinking was shunned and Expitik was the first to go, as she was most nature-based diety on the islands. Once her holy tree was cut down she fled and her followers were massacred by a techno-cult mob. Expitik and the escaping Jutrollags came to Kalimvane and founded and built the basilica in her honor for delivering them through the deluge and Dreadstorms.   
Terris was their loyal leader and powerful in Expitik miracola (miracles). Uftan was his protoge but wanted the miracola faster than Terris would allow. Becoming impatient, Uftan went back to Druvenrog, which in the short 11 years, had become a crawling techo-conurbanation, seeking forgiveness and acceptance. He met secretly with House Grimstok which he made a bargain to become a lackey in the House if he gave up his religion and miracola. He did, for 2 years but longed for Kalimvane, the Jutrollag’s and Expitik. He voyaged back to Kalimvane and stole the automaton **Thegot** from the Grimstok factory. When he reached Kalimvane, Terris was dead, murdered by the native barbarians of **Kwinst**. Uftan was so overcome with pain that he and Thegot, who he had to reprogram, went on a revenge murder spree of the Kwinst. For this Expitik had no pity and banished Uftan from the basilica. Some of the Jutrollags followed Uftan to build the town at the current location it is now. Expitik left the basilica with the rest of the followers to an unknown location. (They left to found the cult of the Storm Kings) She cursed the basilica and the area to be overrun with monsters. Uftan and the rest of the citizens built walls and a moat around the city to help keep the monsters at bay.   
Now Uftan prefers this history to be hidden and never spoken of. Only the original members of the Jutrollags, which there are 3 others, know the story. Everyone else in Kalimvane are newcomers. He has made Kalimvane into the trading center of that region of the Eastern Rim though, because of the monsters, commerce is suffering.   
He wants to make sure that House Grimstok can’t find him. He has a lot of worries on his mind.

The other three members from the Jutrollags are **Vanfang**, who went off to found the thieves guild; **Bildagar**, who is now a hermit in the Boarsback; and **Gregari**, a merchant in the town. By finding and talking to all three of these, and completing the Jutrollag Basilica dungeon, will open up the quest to discover this mystery.

For now, all the player knows is this is a simple trading town. And all they know is that the basilica is a monster haven.

The dungeon adventure:  
Outside the gate is one merchant, **Bleefol**  that sells potions and food. One potion he sells, a life potion, the players should buy many of, which is the best way to do damage to undead **Kawrgam** beast.

The only perceivable entrance is through the bridge as all other angles are guarded by powerful guards called Devourers. Devourer have very high physical combat. They keep a memory of the soul of everyone they kill and add it to their collective knowledge. This information they provide to Charltrolate in his quest for knowledge and search for weaknesses among mortals and gods. Everytime a player is killed by an devourer on the surface, Charltrolate gets more powerful. It is best if the players find this out and avoid all other angles except the broken bridge.

Once

The main cupola is a weathervane to harness the storms. There are four towers that must be switched to send a volt down to Charltrolate[^6] which disconnects him from his devourer fiends.  
This not only weakens him, but also weakens the devourers, and resets the information he knows about the players. In reality he knows your class, and uses spells against certain classes, first taking out clerics, then mages, etc. When the weather vane is invoked, he cannot do this power. For this reason, a minimum of four players must be in the party.

Each tower individually also unlocks a different section of the dungeon to gain access to a special storm item. One tower, that is partially destroyed is particularly hard to get to and might require a rogue to scale.

# **How Ores work**

	Ores in v1 will work as an extra benefit to mining coal ore. Mining a coal ore will have a chance for either a jewelry gem or an ore used for smithing. Crafting starts by combining 2 logs of any kind. Then following the steps of gathering clay, rocks from dirt, twine from grass and sticks from leaves. Then proceeding to make a Kiln to seared bricks to a smeltery for tools.   
	Once this level of crafting is achieved it’s to be assumed a player can learn new ones from their stations without assistance.

# **Item Mechanics**

# 	Items are defined as something that takes up a slot. A slot being a hand, armor, amulet, ring, artifact, bracelet or soulseed. An item can be upgraded according to its type. A hand item is the only exception being able to be upgraded based on what it is. A soulseed can be upgraded infinitely. A ring can be upgraded 5 times. An artifact can be upgraded 3 times. A bracelet can be upgraded 10 times.

	An item can also be enhanced with custom enchants(Subject to change to runes) if it’s a hand or armor item. A custom enchant can be made by a mage using many mana gems and special inks. These enchants can also be bought at high tiers in the stores. An item can be equipped with as many enchants the mage has levels/10.  
**Magic Mechanics**  
	Magic works with crafting skills. A player needs to research magic and increase their proficiency with the element in order to learn the spell. So a Shadow skill needs level 5 or higher proficiency levels. The levels are gained through killing a shadow boss and learning its tome of knowledge. Once the skill is achieved it can be cast without issue. A spellcaster can learn the spell if another spell caster gives it to them. So a fire mage can learn shadow magic if a trade is accepted.  
	This also makes communities of various spell casters useful. That way they can all learn each other's magic so long as their classes align. Therefore is a specified mage attempts to learn a spell from another school they cannot due to being specified a certain way already.  
**World Events**  
	World Events are large scale events that have their own part in the story. Whether it be the discovery of a dungeon for the first time or a boss leaving the dungeon it can drop amazing rewards and event world rewards such as boosters.  
**World Dungeons**  
	World dungeons contain massive amounts of content and bosses. They have amounts of floors equal to the player average level that would be entering. Every 10 floors the players will have a ‘rest area’ where they can build towns and outposts and deal in trades with other players.

# 

# **How Magic works**

Magic is treated as energy ley lines that run through Deluvia. Magic was once used heavily in the Second Age, but had lost usage now that the technology has become prevalent. But after The Cataclysm, the ley lines seem to be stronger than ever encouraging a new generation of mages, and allowing the superstitious and those wary of technology to embrace a more meaningful way of life.

Magery is under seige from the Central Kingdoms, which now effectively comprises of Druvvenrog, which was  instrumental in winning the war against the gods. They also hate all magic and have made it a mission to destroy persecute, or imprison all mages. For now this is limited to their capital and colonies, but the threat that they expand, colonize new territories or feel it is their right to extinguish mages in all of Deluvia is looming.

Magery is still much alive in the outer rim/outlands, which consists of all of Song Tide and the Kingdom of the Wood, and those in The Long Sea that choose to.

New Pallamost, which is now a lap dog to Druvenrog purports neutrality in the magery debate, but everyone knows they still will report mages to their overseers, The Corporation Dominion (Druvenrog). For now New Pallamost is lucky enough to be allowed to worship their old gods.

Magery is controlled by the Denizen plugin.

Spells and skills are very similar as far as game mechanics goes. The main difference is that spells use **mana**.  
The other distinction is bard spells. They are called **spell songs**, and are enacted as a song but still drain mana.  
Another distinction are cleric spells, which are **prayer spells**. They are almost exactly the same as spells, but often, instead of inflicting damage, they affect a party, or an area of effect, or are involved with the miracles of their patron deity. A cleric/priest/paladin/druid’s mana is called **faith** but it is the same mechanic.  
The more important main difference is how they are in lore. Magic is mysterious and evokes supernatural abilities; same with spell songs; but skills are things that people learn with practice in the normal world. These skills, however, are feats that are above what a normal person can learn in the world and can sometimes be heroic. 

When a player chooses the Mage class, it opens up a path to learn a myriad of spells.  
NPCs will know a player is a mage class and offer them the chance to learn spells from them if they don’t know it already. Generally, less powerful spells are found in beginning areas, close to where the player starts, but that does not preclude from learning a very advanced spells. The main thing preventing them from learning an advanced skills, is if that advanced skill has a **prerequisite**. Prerequisites follow a natural path of advancement. Another thing that might prevent them from using a spell is that their mana is not high enough.  
Some spells that have a prerequisite will need the prerequisite to be at a certain level before they can learn it.

Once a spell is learned, it will show up in a player’s spell book. They can then cast it.  
The chance of the spell successfully being cast is based on the player’s **magery** skill. Every player has a magery skill, and it goes up naturally from casting spells.

**Mana** is the amount of magical energy it takes from the mage to cast the spell. It is a direct amount based on the player’s intelligence which the player can raise through spending **attribute points**. Mana can be increased above intelligence usually with equipment bonuses, or buffs.  
The **mana regeneration** rate is based on passive **meditation**, which is another skill that ever player has, and is raised through use. Use is defined as when mana is re-gained after it being spent from casting a spell. Active meditation is when a player chooses to activate their meditation skill, but they cannot do anything during that time and must remain still and concentrate. Active  meditation is much faster at gaining mana than passive meditation.

Spells  are affected by a **build up**, which is a time that is from when a player casts the spell until it actually is cast. Spells can have a **distance** limit. Spells have a recovery time, called a **cooldown**, until that, or any other spell can be cast again. Many spells have a **damage** that they inflict if they are successful. All of these spell mechanics/stats can be raised with equipment or other buffs.  
Many of these factors can be raised when the spell is leveled up. A player can level up a skill by using **skill points**. Skill points are found throughout the gain through exploration, from completing quests, etc.   
Spells are often in the category of one of the **12 elements**. For example, a fire ball is in the fire elemental magic. Some skills are percentage of 2 or more elements depending on what lore they have.   
The player that a spell is cast against has **magical elemental resistances** which have a chance to reduce the damage done by the spell.

The Mage class gets their skills from talking to NPCs and learning them or finding spells in quests, or other various ways of introducing them to that spell. 

If a player specializes in a certain elemental magic, they get a bonus. They can specialize in one by making it over 50% of the spells they have learned and/or leveled up in as that elemental. For example, if they have over 50% of their spells in fire, they get **Fire Aspect** and then get a bonus of 5% for all fire elemental spells. A spell that is considered a fire elemental spell is one that has over 70% of its damage as fire damage.   
The more the player has leveled up in a spell counts toward this calculation as well. For example, a fire ball that is leveled to 5, counts 5 times as much towards this calculation as another fire spell that is leveled at 1\.

This is explained in the Magery tab of the mechanics spreadsheet.  
https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1P955ScPAHCnSaXpYfGhXnIQFvqa\_WQ\_Aa3FkBUyKdSM/edit\#gid=195549530

If not given any further clarification, a mage is known as an Elementalist, and most of their spells are to cause damage in some way to a being.

Components or reagents in magic spells  
Corpse nettle  
Feainnewedd  
wolfsbane

# **Player Towns**

In this section we will define what it is for players to have their own town. As of version 1.0, this is a big feature of our game and should be rich and rewarding.

We use the custom (coded in Denizen) **Stronghold** plugin to manage most of the town building and protections.

## NPC combat

One mechanic of SteamFront will be RTS (real time strategy) battle and city-building components. We utilize Towny for city management, but players will be able to buy pre-made structures from NPCs with in-game money that will make their town stronger.

Players will be able to buy towers, houses, armories, that will add to defense and attack abilities of their towns and units.  Some are decorative, some are functional.  
Each can be upgraded for better results. Some have requirements.

All structures require the player to have the **Builder** Profession Class. (it does not need to be the mayor)

We will have to make sure that this mechanic is not too Overpowered, hence the class limitation above. That is, we want to make sure a player cannot wipe out another player easily. One option is to have town leaders Opt in to raiding warfare. Another is to have a grace period, or everything at Town level (20 residents) and below is unable to participate in raiding warfare. Or a combination of these.

## Structures

#### Structure types:

1. Tower \- able to put archers or ballistas on to defend town  
   1. Upgrades:   
      1. Larger/stronger towers. Requirement: Foundry  
      2. Can add notifications to alarm owner when town is under siege while offline (eg. text message)  
2. Walls \- adds strength to hinder a siege  
   1. Upgrades: Taller/stronger walls. Requirement: Foundry, Masonry  
3. Great Hall \- Allows for advanced structure upgrades  
   1. Upgrades: gives diplomacy points, and Leaderboard points  
4. Barracks \- Trains NPC troops ( 1 \* modifier  per day)   
   1. Upgrades: each level determines type of troop  
   2. Level 1: foot soldiers \- a start  
   3. Level 2: swordsmen (requires blacksmith) good all-around soldier  
   4. Level 3: Pikemen (requires blacksmith and lumbermill) good for defending calvary  
   5. Level 4: Macemen (requires blacksmith and lumbermill) \- good against armored troops  
   6. Level 5: Archers (requires lumbermill and archery range) good for and against NPCs in towers  
   7. Level 6: Crossbowmen (requires lumbermill, blacksmith and archery range). Good in towers and against calvary  
   8. Level 7: Calvary (requires stables and blacksmith).  Fast  
   9. Level 8: Paladin/Knight \- converts a calvary \- Deadly and fast  
5. Lumber Mill \- auto lumbers wood from surrounding forests  
   1. Upgrades  
      1. Can double lumber harvesting for certain periods  
6. Iron Mining camp \- auto mines certain ores from surrounding quarries  
   1. Upgrades  
      1. Can double ore mining for certain periods  
7. Blacksmith \- builds weapons for your troops (consumes iron)  
   1. Upgrades  
      1. Consumes less iron for weapons  
      2. Stronger weapons  
8. Foundry \- for stronger buildings and siege weapons. Requires blacksmith.   
   Having a player in the town that is **Engineer** Profession Class builds them faster and stronger.  
   1. Siege Engines:  
      1. Level 1: Boiling oil pot \- defends walls against scaling troops  
      2. Level 2: Battering ram \- to take down doors  
      3. Level 3: Catapults \- take down walls  
      4. Level 4: Ballista \- fires large missiles for defense and offense  
      5. Level 5: Siege Tower \- aids in scaling walls.  
      6. Level 6: Drawbridge \- removes bridge for defense (max length 32 blocks)  
9. Archery range- allows for archers to be trained. Requires lumbermill  
10. Stables \- allows for calvary to be trained. Requires lumbermill, blacksmith.

#### Structure Mechanics:

The player that wants to build these special structures, must first have the **Builder** Profession.  
They can get this from training under any NPC builder, usually from a big server town. They pay the NPC some money (e.g. 320 coin) and then are then the Builder class and can start learning that group of skills. Note, they do not need any skills yet to build. Just the Class. The skills that they can level up in just, give bonuses to and more options to builds.

They can then find plans to buy from NPCs across Deluvia for the above structures. They cost as much as the materials would plus the know-how of the designer. Something around 500,000 coin is reasonable for a tower. The player then gets access to the “tower01” command, or whichever structure they bought.  
The player goes back to their town and to the location they want to build. The command has instructions and size dimensions. They command /tower01 and a glass tower in the shape of the tower gets put in the location of the player for positioning. They can then command /tower01confirm, /tower01rotate or /tower01cancel. The former then puts the schematic in the same place the glass example was; /tower01rotate rotates it 90 degrees (they can do this 3 times; and /tower01cancel of course undoes and lets them start over. Once they do /tower01confirm, the permission is taken away. Worldguard is also part of the script to make a region around the tower against grief and the owner of the region the player that placed it.  
There are then worldscript flags that monitor that region for calculations for this whole mechanic.   
For example, if another player tries to break a block on this tower, certain things can happen. There are algorithms for stats based on other factors that determine the tower’s strength. 

#### Structure Repair

There is a skill under the Builder Class that is **building inspection** and **building repair**. Building inspection will tell the builder what level of repair the structure is in. Building repair will repair the structure. That mechanic works like this:

* Level 1: The building is just placed and impervious to attack. It has WG protection for 1 week.  
* Level 2: (Week 2)The building’s blocks are able to be destroyed after 1000 (\* modifiers) hits with WG protection randomly phasing in and out. It is sometimes invincible (1/3rd chance)  
* Level 3: (Week 3\) The building’s blocks are able to be destroyed after 1000 (\*  modifiers) hits  
* Level 4: (Week 4\) The building’s blocks are able to be destroyed after 120 hits (\*  modifiers)  
* Level 5: (Week 5\) The building’s blocks lose all protection and are just normal  
* Level 6: (Week 6\) The building’s blocks randomly turn to gravel, a few per day

If the player that is the keeper of the building/that built it uses their building repair skill, It costs (1100 \* repair-Level \* tower-size)  coin to move  it up one level.  (e.g. 6600 coin from Level 6 to Level 5\)

The enemy player’s attack skills are modifiers that can add into the structures demise. For example, there is a high-level siege attack skill that can move structures down a repair level.

## Troop Notes

Troops are better controlled if the general (player commanding the troops) has the **General/Leader** Profession Class and upgrades skills such as **tactics**.

Note: Players can always hire mercenaries instead of training their own troops, but they are expensive. A mercenary is a specific, unique NPC that can be hired to help and rally troops, or just fight on their own.  
NPC soldiers are usually never as good as an average siege player or PvPer.  
Many skills under the *General* class add to the NPC soldiers abilities

Troops consume the town coffers. 10 coin per level, per troop, per day. (e.g. a Paladin will consume 80 coin per day; a full unit will consume 80 \* 16 \= 1280 coin) (1 unit \= 16 troops)  
If the money is not there, the troops disband and are lost to the player and the player must start over to train them up.

#### Controlling Troops

Troops are controlled by a player that has a **General/Leader** profession. If they are not controlled, troops are auto AI, which is then only for defense. They will attack anyone that is not a member of the town or an ally of the town when the town is under attack. They will only be able to stay in their town and not siege another town.

A General can lead 1 troop per the player’s General level to a max of 16 per unit type. (8 \* 16 \= 128 max per general if the player has their General Class leveled to 128). The General’s troops will defend the General and attack however the General attacks. The squads will automatically be broken into their unit type (e.g. swordsmen, archers), and that will be the command the general uses  
Commands:

* /archers attack \- attacks the block the general clicks on next. If other NPCs/Players/Mobs are in the way, they will attack them first.  
* /archers stop \- unit stops their attacks and will do nothing.  
* /archers defend \- unit will only defend general and themselves.  
* /archers retreat \- units will turn in the opposite direction they are facing and run for  30 \- **confidence** skill seconds and then get tped back to their spawn point in the base.  
* /archers mopup \- units will attack anything but friendlies  
*   
* /allunits attack \- the same commands can be used for all units to send all of them to do the same thing. Potentially sending 128 troops to all do the same thing.


Different General skills can add to their troops skills. (e.g. attack distance, speed), as well as skills to counter other enemy Generals and enemy troops

## Trade Ports

If a town reaches Demiburghal  level (30 residents), they will get a free trade port route with any of the server cities. They must buy a ship from a NPC boatyard for in-game money.  
Each level thereafter gets another route. At Nation level they can have a route to anywhere on the map. Each Nation level gets one more route to anywhere they choose. For each ship, the player (mayor) can choose how much to charge for passage to customers and make money for the town. This port/wharf comes with the same structure repair as outlined above.

## Sea Warfare . . . coming soon . . .

“The old faiths light their candles all about, but burly Truth comes by and puts them out.”

# The Player Path

### Option 1 (Meruk Dialog):

The player starts out in Meruk’s cave  
Meruk: Ah so you’ve arrived.   
Deluvia, our world has been springing up new beings and some of them arrive here to me.  
What shall I call you? Hero, Mortal? Traveler?  
This is a harsh world, and it seems to have gotten harsher in recent times and it is no wonder that Deluvia has conjured you here to  this spot in the world, the cave in which I hide, watching Rothigport, that town down the path; and I wait for a sign.  
Are you this sign?  
All twelve of us original elder sages are recluse, yet, some of us remain close enough to the  Ecuneme to chronicle what storms are to come upon the beings of Deluvia.  
We hope that you can help us but whatever path you choose is up to you.  
We’re glad you’re here.  
Oh how rude of me, let me not get ahead of myself.  
I am Meruk, the sage of scholars and Keeper of the Deluvic Bardsong, an ancient tome chronicling our land.  
What is a scholar doing living in a cave you ask?  
Ha ha ha. Fair enough.  
All of us sages, have used our specialities to their height at one point or another during this Age of Kings, but things are not always safe for us after the Great War between the gods and the mortals, and we found new occupations in dank locations; but I do still, however, keep my books.  
I have written extensively about Rothigport and Songtide lately. Songtide being this realm, far away from the powerful civilizations, and Rothigport being one of its main commercial centers.  
I brought my family here after living in Druvvenrog as one of their top scholars. The Druvs and Venrogs are mortals too, but things have gotten hostile there for those of us seeking truth and understanding of the Great Severing. I still sneak back into Druvvenrog, to visit their libraries and to watch a skiffrunner race once and awhile, but as time goes on, this dark hole in a rock is all I have left.

1. Tell me more about how you came to Songtide.

   Me and my son met the fishermen with a few boats and a few docks in the middle of the harbor. They did this to keep away from the land barbarians that were afraid of water. We helped build the town, all out of wood, as it was the most humble of materials for a humble race of Anthorans, of which I am one. Modrik, my son, built the causeway that connected the town to the land and more pilgrims came. The Blackthorn Brothers, Merkti Prigtoon and other industrialists who cared not for magic, but for their own profits. The town grew fast.

   

   Now the young folk of town are again being attracted to magic. But this time it is different; it is a much darker form which they find alluring. The elders think it is just a fad, but pay attention and let me know what comes from it.

   

   Yes I dabble in magic as well. See. \[Meruk casts a fire touch spell\]

   I am by no means as powerful as the Four Arch Mages which watch over Song Tide and keep a veil of protection warding off evil. In fact building is even protected by their spells and pioneers must travel out among The Long Sea to find their own area to build the next stronghold or empire.

   Seek out my fellow Deluvians in Rothigport and in the islands outside of it and they can offer you help. Also be wary of certain ones of them, as more nefarious being come and lurk to steal and harm.

2. Why did you leave Druvvenrog?

   Druvvenrog was getting too dangerous for believers in the Old Gods, and for those of us from the Ancient Ways. It is a great place to make a fortune as your back is getting stabbed.

3. Who are the 12 Sages?

   We are the first mortals to crawl out of the gapping Omphalos, created by Deluvia herself we spread in the 12 directions progenerating the 12 races. If you are curious about this land, I have no doubt you will get to meet them all eventually.

4. What is this Savior you are awaiting?

   The devout from this region and what good gods are left have pled for Deluvia to suppress the Severing she has unleashed, including floods, wars, plagues and threats from within our own species. We hope that a new set of Leaders can help this land in whichever direction they see fit, as our time here is nearing an end.

I have bent your ear enough and I will see you again soon, I am sure.  
I can teleport you down to Rothigport or another nearby port to start your adventure.

1. First can you teach me that fancy fire touch spell?

   Yes, indeed, spells can be useful. Talk to more mages out there in the world to learn more.

Would you like to to to Rothigport, just out in the harbor here, or

1. Krakencay, a pirate town just out on the edge of the Songtide  
2. Kalimvane, a large island town that is far enough away to still be anonymous  
3. Gweftshire, a town in a ealm steeped in ancient magic of the faeriefolk  
4. Runesbrook, a small town in the west of Songtide

Albus: Hail and well met stranger\!  
What be thy tide?  
Heading to Rothigport?  
Oh me? I am just a wanderer who has lived out in these parts for quite awhile.  
But I needed to start a new life too as it seems the dangers spread and there is not many places a quiet existence can be lived.

Sit and stay warm by my fire as I tell you more.

Ah you are new? Let me give you some tips for your journey ahead.  
\[ *show cutscene of rothigport*\]

North, down this path will bring you to Rothigport, which has grown fast in my time living in the midst of it.

A quaint town of humble origins, but be wary of some of the new industrialists in town, willing to take advantage of newcomers. And unsavory smugglers and robbers are starting to find refuge there as well.

If you can get to the inner harbor talk to Lathander, as he is always excited to meet new folk.  
Next to him is the bank where you can safely store your goods, and docked just there is a ship of Ori Moonsails, who can take you to the Outlands to blaze your own trail in the new lands.   
Be careful out there though as those lands are a bit wild, but once you can secure your own little town, you will find safety and solace there at least.

I’m glad you’re here mysterious hero. We certainly need one in these times. Whether it be a masterful blacksmith, or a blade-wielding legend, or just a simple farmer, the more beings we can have to keep our race from becoming extinguished from those that wish to have it undone, the better.

Go, and meet your fellow travelers in Rothigport, and do come back and visit and tell me of your exploits\!

Oh you want me to teach you something? I think I have time for that. This stew is not going to be finished for a few moonticks.

Hmmm, let me ponder. . .  
Oh\! I shall show you my favorite, a blocking defense. Quite useful when running into the wrong creature out here.

There now you know something of this. Just time out your swings to stop an attack, or I hear, if practiced enough in the art, can send the missile back at the sender\! How about that. Go and try

I suppose you require a physical form to properly communicate, now don't you?  
I suppose it's not a difficult task for me to grant another spirit a form.  
Tell me young one. What is your preference?  
Oh yes, you can't speak. I can read your thoughts now. So tell me  
	Elf  
	Orc  
	Dwarf  
	Human

Quite the option you have chosen. Give me a moment and we will get you sorted.  
The man's voice gets harder to hear…

*(if elf)*  
Why must the spirits choose elves... I might as well make them an Orc for that\! I suppose they just want to live longer…

*(if orcs)*  
Why must the spirits choose Orcs of all things... I might as well make them an Elf for that\!

*(If dwarf)*  
Why must the spirits choose Dwarves... I might as well make them an Human for that\!

*(if human)*  
My, finally a Human has appeared... Something simple.

*(if human)*  
Open your eyes.  
That wasn't so hard now was it?

*(any other race)*  
Open your eyes.  
Great\! Now I get to scorn the one who decided to ask for such a difficult race\!

*(Player asks)* Where am I?  
I found you here in the mountains near Bardtown, the center of Songtide\!

Bardtown is probably where you should go. I hear many stories of how accepting and cheerful they are. Hopefully you don't die and become a spirit again there.

(Player asks) Who am I?  
Who? I don't know. I found you here as a spirit in my cave.

(Player asks)) What am I?  
You cannot tell me you just had me give you such a marvelous form only for you to not know what it is\!

(Player, if not human,  asks) What do you mean scorn?  
You don't quite seem to understand the task you asked me of. I had to sit here for days creating the form of *(whichever race the player picked)*

I suppose it’s water under the bridge now.

Do you have any other questions before you let me back into my isolation?  
*(player says)* I will leave now.

Excellent\! Now leave me back to my meditation\!  
I highly recommend going to Bardtown. It will be of much assistance.

END MERUK DIALOG.  
Player heads down path toward Bardtown

[The player then gets to Krizzdo which offers to shoot them into the top of Bardtown](#bookmark=kix.7au98lx70tzh)

\=================================================================  
The player starts out in Rothigport on the east side of the harbor in front of the Fisher Guild house. They are near Ori Moonsails boat, so they could take passage to Padula Anchorite which will get them close to the wilderness

They are also close to Lathander McFenn who can give them some starting tips and some starting gear. Rothigport is “The City of Wood” since it was founded on timber trade and is built on docks which are made of wood; so Lathander gives them a set of wood tools and weapons.

Lathander, besides for the tools, can give them a little overview of the world,  
A decent amount about Songtide, and then more detail about Rothigport

In Song Tide, creatures will not attack the player unless the player attacks them. Once that type of creature is attacked by the player enough, that type of creature will consider the player an enemy and then always attack them on sight.   
If they are in the Outlands it is different. In the Outlands, if the player is new for 2 days, the creatures will not attack them, but only defend themselves. Once the player is past 2 (real world) days old hostile creatures will attack the player.  
In Song Tide all creatures live in relative peace, except for the Snarlbush Formoris who raid ships that pass through. The creatures of Song Tide are more sentient and intelligent than most other realms. Creatures are stronger and have better loot, but the consequences of killing them is often higher. For instance, the player will likely lose karma, unless they are at war with that creature. Creatures that are allied with the slain creature may find out about it and spread the word of the players aggression. The gods that the slain creature worships may look down upon you and curse you in other ways later in the game. 

In the city of Rothigport, the player can meet some introductory characters that teach them things.  
**Magprythymo** the Crow Mage \- Can give the player the class of mage and teach them the Gust spell  
**Vermardi** the Mouse Thief- Can give the player the rogue class and teach them one stealing skill  
**Horgavid** , the Badger can give the player the warrior class and teach them one fighting skill  
**Pardieu** the Fox cleric can give the player the cleric class and teach them one prayer  
The player can only learn these four classes here and must find the Drifter class and Ranger class outside of the city docks.  
The player can also learn fletching/bowmaking, blacksmithy, herbalism,   
The trades of gardening can be learned elsewhere

To get more learned spells:

	The Forest Seers: Blossom, 

	Rosage: Spark

Fritz Lafrafop is the barkeep at the Whistlepig Pub at the NE side of the harbor in Rothigport

He is a generous host and amiable at most times. But if you get to know him well, he will start to open up and talk about his dismay at his daughter Penny’s state. She sits at the bridge and looks out for her lost lover, Braid, who went off to fight in the wars of the Central Kingdom colonies. He ever came back, and was reported dead, by survivors. Penny was lost and could not recover. Fritz thought she might throw herself off the bridge and succumb to the depths of the harbor, but she just stand on top and looks North, the direction he left and where he would return from. 

Now Penny was given a ring from Braid, when he promised he would return. Penny took this deep to her heart and thought the promise was a immutable desire that would be fulfilled. When she dropped the ring into the harbor from her many nights looking out from the high bridge, her forlorn increased and she was in a heartbroken stupor. 

Fritz knows of his daughter’s fiance’s murderers and is looking to mobilze a small group of fighters to go and avenge her loss. He is looking for the best warriors in Rothigport. He is not one, but he will send this group across The Long Sea to at least find out more information about his death and bring rest to his soul.

He gives hints to this, but he won’t activate until you bring him the ring, and are part of party of at least four. The more the better he says. He will commandeer a boat, that will bring you to the Central Kingdoms colonies, outside the Phalloworn Mines, where the Phalloworn Battle of took place only 2 moons ago.

The mystery to find his exact killers is a quest and will introduce the players to the Central Kingdoms. 

## Pool of Haught

	The Water Elemental Mistforborl \- Waterball, or geyser (if they already have waterball) He is in the Pool of Haught which the entrance can be found west of Rothigport in a cave in the forest. If the player follows the northern coast, going north and west of Rothigport, they will find a small cove with a small water fall. At the source of that water fall is a small cave which leads to the Pool of Haught. 

Though Mistborforl is not modest himself, lets the players offer to the Shrine of Purity. If enough mortals do this, it may spare Rothigport from the Tempest which would overtake it.

Mistborforl was once one of the Guardians of the Great Forge, which is now occupied by the technopriests of Druvvenrog (and renamed Dane’s Crucible after the High Technopriest) when they defeated Skragamor, keeper of the Flame, and sent him deeper into the Abyss of the Nether.

When the player enters the Pool of Dissolute  they can make their way down to the other side, when they enter

Maxims etched into the stone:

“West of the City of Wood\<\&nl\>Rests a pond that could\<\&nl\>a mortal dive and swim\<\&nl\>and arrive to find him in a cavern lush\<\&nl\>the Guardian of scornful gush”  
Given to Rosage  
“

“Mine enemies be scorched by the lightning and tossed by the Tempest. May the pure be spared from the Storm”

By reciting this command phrase to open secrets

By completing this, it is one step of the Virtues quest

He has high HP and shoots a greater water ball.

It took the fishing industry to be slowed down, to finally take notice of the changes to this area of Deluvia. The fisherman were not happy that the fish weren’t biting or showing up in their nets. Had all the fish been fished? It was the Mystic Rosage the Potion Maker who first consulted the Oracle at Omphalos to gain some answers. The Ley Lines that run through Deluvia are being changed by Deluvia herself with the Great Unstiching or Great Severing. This exemplary work by Rosage, who was just not yet a veteran mage, gained the attention of Nax Hollum. Nax made Rosage his apprentice and they, together, set forth to discover more about mysteries of this Great Sundering.

One of the disturbances causing this, that Rosage or Nax or any of the Arch Mages of Song Tide don’t know about, is the defeat of the Great Skragamor, molten titan of the Nether. It sent  Deluvia into an unbalance. Another disturbance is the rise of the mortals. The mortals are descendents of Deluvia, but they have fallen out of balance with nature. One of these reasons is certainly Druvvenrog, but Rothigport itself and the pride of the officials has also driven this. No mortals realize this yet.

## The Dirt Kingdom

The Dung Beetle Dirt Kingdom

Stercortrupes \- The Beetle Prince  
The player can get to the Carapacubicular Humilitas  (The chamber of Humility) by the Deep Caves of Song Tide.This is part of a much larger cavern network called the **Fungal Underground.** The entrance is at the far end of the Glistal Cave and the altar entrance is located there and through a tunnel they enter The **Chamber of Meeks** where they will immediately see the Ponds of Penitence. They are actually the Shamelshroom, so called by the stercus beetlefolk, and can increase a player’s karma and release some sins from other quests. In this chamber they can also collect nectar from some of the mega flora if they need. The draggleflap swarms overhead usually leaving the player alone  
**Meeks** is a Badger Clan druid monk and acolyte of **Putref** one of the mycelium goddesses. Meeks is an Anthoran who seeks isolation, but helps players that have come into these caverns. She can teach the cleric spell of **Decomposition**, which allows corpses to be absorbed into the soil immediately. (useful to keep necromancers from using the corpses). She also can give a mushroom tea that gives agility and staves off exhaustion for the day.  
Meeks will buy rotten flesh, mushrooms, or many of the drops in the chamber.  
Meeks is not in his hut when the player first arrives. But if they have collected mugstool, and put it in a bowl and cook it into soup on his stove, he loves the smell and will come to his hut to get it. He is grateful to you for making his favorite meal , Mugstool Stew, and will now help you.  
Meek also gives the magical item **The Wand of Soil’s Calm**, which does dirt magic damage, physical damage, chance at Bury spell, **Cancel Quake** cleric spell, and temporarily lowers fame and charisma while being held.  The player can attain this Wand if they fulfill Meek’s request to tell her brother, Roganth, that she is safe and not to worry about her, but not to tell her where she is. That she is on her own quest of purity and humility in service of Putref. Roganth is in Rothigport and if the player brings him one of Meek’s mushroom, that will unlock the wand. Meek’s other request is that the player give alms to the poor, at least one silver to 10 different beggars in Rothigport to show generosity and humility. Both of these are optional, but must be done in order for Meeks to give the wand.

*There also exists elsewhere in the world*  
*The **Wand of Soil’s Ire**, a wand that when held boosts the player’s charisma and fame temporarily, which can be useful with NPCs. When attained, though, will make the Dirt Elemental even angrier and more difficult. The Beetles will also think less of you and help you less. This wand enrages the Dirt Elemental Clodhaught if you ever knowingly attained it and are in his presence. This Wand can be found in the Dungeon of Vanity and Corruption (Livivinox Maculagnz Hor)*

A maxim is etched into the stone at Meek’s Hut

“Be grounded, prideful traveler. Know thy measure, Study thyself and Be Aware of thine place for confidence brings ruin.”

**Chamber of Perf** \- The Town of Stercuswarth, where is also the Altar of Perf. The demigod Perf was born of **Bref** the god of mud. Perf is the demigod of filth and decay and takes player’s vanity and absorbs it to recycle it back into the energy of Deluvia. Perf is a known god in Song Tide, but Perf does not wish not wish glory, but in fact seeks lowliness. This Chamber is named after him for he is the patron god of the Beetles. If you have not heard of him, he is pleased by this.

Another maxim in this chamber  
“Yield to the Storms of Dust and bow to the Gods of Decay. Know thy filth, bury thy vanity at the altar of Perf.”

The dirt elemental Clodhaught was conjured by Deluvia to keep Rothigport in check for its growing pride. Rothigport was founded on a sense of pragmatism and humility. He does not exist to harm or destroy Rothigport, but just as a check for its growing vanity and haughtiness. He took the form of dirt as a compliment to Rothigports respect for the sea. Also, Rothigport adopted the Virtue of Humility since that is the patron virtue of the Anthorans (Badger, Fox, mouse etc). The Anthorans were also formed out of mud by the gods and sages old fables say. When the water was separated to form the harbor around Rothigport, the dirt was left to do the work of building the town.There is a saying that a Rothigportian is not afraid to get their hands dirty.  
Rothigport was founded on hard work and Humility and respect for the sea. For 100 generations the Gods protected them from the sea.

This is Clodhaught’s way of offering redemption for Rothigport and its growing pride, but only if the residents of Song Tide do some penitent work, and that begins in Carapacubicular Humilitas. Clodhaught was summoned as a foil to Prigtoon, as a representative of the greed and rising pride and sins in this old town. 

The Stercus Beetle colony value humility as a virtue and hard work, burrowing tunnels under Song Tide, but for little reward. Though they are aware of Rothigport and Anthorans, they are unaware of Anthoran politics and ambitions. They feel the physical rumblings of those walking above, but make it none of their business. 

The Stercus colony are abiding to any visitors but are especially sensitive to lofty and vainful conceits. The higher your charisma and/or fame, the less they will help you. In fact, if too high, they will attack you until you are out of Stercuswarth limits.

The Path of the Humble:  
Beg for money in Rothigport \- give to 10 beggars

Seek the Shepherd \- There is Croknard, the shepherd out in the field with his sheep. If the player can help him herd his sheep they get this checked off

Ritual of Humility \- The Altar of Humility  
For it is always haughtiness that destroys those in power

The Dung Beetle Prince can give the player the Nadel’s Nostrum, a cure-all potion. He encourages the player to eat some dung. This also increases the player humility score.

If the player enters Clodhaught’s chamber without any introduction, he attacks them as he feels they don’t below in the Fungal Underground. Only the most humble of creatures can come to him. He sleeps for eternities without one visitor just feeling the tremors of mortals ambitions above.

If the player has an introduction from the Dung Beetle Prince, then he will offer to challenge them to a duel.

“I am light and I am heavy. I am strong enough to hold up a castle. I am fragile enough to be blown away in the wind. I am an anchor. I am a home. I am a sponge. I am one substance made of many different things. I am loose enough to flow like a river. I am solid as a mountain. I can be fertile. I can be barren. I am living and I am dead.”

Clodhaught, the Dirt Elemental casts quake, and quicksand. The player can cancel quake with the Wand of Soil’s Calm. If they time their jump right, they can miss the damage from quake. Quick sand will pull the player under slowly and make them very slow. They can move out of the way of the area if they are quick enough. If caught in the quicksand, they can counter act it with a speed poison. Of course if they save with a high enough dirt magic resistance, the spell will have less effect. Clodhaught is very slow so they should be able to see these coming.

The dirt elemental has to be beaten by simply lowering its HP. Water damage and poison damage will slow it down quite a bit to give a break for healing or gaining mana.

The dirt elemental cannot be killed but only subdued. He is just testing the players ability. Upon defeat he will give the player a choice between teaching them the quake or quicksand spell,  or the Ground Splitter warrior ability, or a mudstone gem

Mobs to fight  cordyceps maggot, slogbeast, draggleflap

Loot to get,

 maggot drops fly larva (egg), or cordyceps or slimeball, or bonemeal, or rotten flesh or night vision potion, or compost, or mushroom and 5 xp

Slogbeast drops mudblock or dungball or dripstone block or potion of slowness or soul soil mucous ; or compost and 10 xp

Draggleflap drops lingering potion of luck, or blue dye, or blood moss, or glow berries, or glowstone dust or draggleflap wing and 15xp

Mantis Tribe, sisters of dreams. The Fungal Underground seeks balance and  provides an immunity to the Infection coming from above in the Overworld

Moonberries

## Cavern (Dungeon) Vanitas – Livivinox Maculagnz Hor (poison dungeon)

The entrance is located just south of Mage town, or just north of Rystrilmyl  
The domain of Ratatoskel the Squirrel the sly messenger demon of poison. He considers himself the glorious champion of the Fungal Underground. He believes he is the greatest of demon gods, even though he was banished by Sifaneus from the aether to Vanitas to rule as a meer demi-god. He has gone crazy since living among the snakes and the rats and worms of the deep soil.  
The dungeon is an old poison mine and Mathor Dust production facility.  
Here a lot of dirt magic or dirt items will help the player to absorb poison damage. A high Humility score will help as well. Completing the Dirt Kingdom area first will help.

The mine had an explosion of the Mathor Dust several generations ago and all the workers had been poisoned and were presumed dead. The mine was sealed. The Goddess **Noxhortes** aided the monsters that formed because of the leaked poison as it was one of her goals for the blight to spread and affect Fecundia. She feeds Ratatoskel’s delusions about taking the highest position among the gods someday.

The player descends through the snake entrance mouth and goes down a winding passage where, at the bottom, they can see the central chamber mine. 

One way Noxhortes and Rataotskel plan on spreading her blight curses is with poison acorns called  the Allzeer Acorns. Ratatoskel buries them in the tunnels in the Fungal Undergrowth, hoping one takes root. Ratatoskel uses this tunnel from to sneak to the toplands on his way to the underdark

Here the player can defeat Vanitas and gain passage to Fecundia as these passages lead underneath the Great Tree Urd Drasil.  
Vanitas is a reminder of the morality of the creatures of Deluvia. This is the Age of Mortals after all, and Noxhortes, being a petty goddess, keeps this energy of Vanitas and Poison beneath Song Tide as a staging ground for Blight and destroying mortal knowledge and bringing mortal civilization back to a primal state. She keeps a bonfire in the chamber for mortals to come throw their knowledge into. In exchange throwing a book into the fire, she will unlock poison magic for the player.

Symbols include skulls, hourglass, wilting flowers, snakes/serpents, corruption, defilement 

The first chamber is Ophidi’s descent. The long walk is supposed to contemplate one’s mortality

The 8 poisons

* Blightox (dirt)  
  * \- Decay spell  
* Venomox (stone)  
  * Wyvern poison  
  * Purple worm poison  
  * Spider venom  
  * Snake venom  
  * Infectious Strike skill  
  * Serpent Arrow skill  
  * Monsters: snakes   
  * Paralyze spell  
* Mephinox (air)  
  * \- the entrance is in the ventilation shaft above the main room to the north west end. This vent stopped bringing fresh air in, which poisoned all the mine workers and released poisons into the chambers making the monsters extra mean

# Character Profiles:

**Lathander McFenn**

Objectives: Lathander loves

## Quests

Quests are an organized way to give players something to do and be a part of the story in SteamFront. Though the word “quests” is usefully to talk about these goals, the word will not be used in the game except for a player’s epic journey to their ultimate goal. Words like Objectives, Achievements, Missions, etc. might be more useful words to use. In the game it is useful to talk about these things as participating in part of the story.

#### Type of Quests

* Combat \- defeat mobs  
* Agility \- parkour, scale walls, dodge boulders  
* Puzzles \- physical areas to manipulate items or blocks to find a solution  
* Maze \- navigate a maze  
* Riddles \- intellectual puzzles.   
* Lore Knowledge \- using areas of the story of Deluvia to find a solution. This can also relate to riddles  
* Deliver \- bring an item to an area or NPC. This could involve supply/demand goods  
* Escort \- escort an NPC to a new area  
* Obtain \- Fetch an item, or obtain a skill

A combination of any of the above. This list is not rigid and should be added to.

Quests and dungeons should always contain 

1. combat component  
2. narrative component  
3. puzzle component  
4. reward component. 

Each room of a dungeon, for example, can reinforce and contribute to these 4 components.

Quests will be added constantly and epic quests will be added at each Update.

Note that the game is about understanding the world and using the lore to solve problems; about being inquisitive and about rewarding the player for being curious about the people and places in this world. Objects are not just about stat gain, and quests are not just about gear and leveling. The goal is the change the way the player thinks about the world and get them to engage with it as a living thing rather than a game object. It’s also to encourage curiosity. It was built to get the player not only searching out the world in terms of physical space but also trying different interactions with NPCs in order to discover the historical or mythological space of this world.

#### Examples of Quest hierarchy

* Epic Quest \- quests that change the narrative and direction of the world  
* Personal Journey \- something that is unique to the characters but also can permeate into the world’s narrative  
* Race Quest \- each race gets an large quest that helps them discover the lore of their race and reunite with others of their race  
* Class Quests \- Each class will have at least one master quest to help the player learn their class skills and follow the paths of that class.   
* Class Specialization Quest \- In addition to normal class quest, when a player gets near maxing their levels in a class, they will be guided through another quest which helps them specialize a proficiency or dual class. For example, a rogue can now become an assassin and get uber assassin skills unlocked, but can no longer general thieve as well. That is to say, once a player starts to specialize in their class, the general class skills get neglected and are maxed and will not be as powerful as their specialization skills.  
* Playable Area Quests \- Each playable area will have at least one large quest that has to do with the lore of that area. For example. There should be a dungeon in each area that can be solved and grinded. There should also be a non-combat based quest in each area. Keep in mind making both solo quests and party-focused quests. Party-focused quests encourage each class for their participation.  
* Many medium-sized quests that involve, lore, economy and finding unique items.  
* Daily Quests \- small quests that reset daily that can reward the players for completing them  
* Economy Quests \- These are built into the supply and demand, but can be used by the administration to manipulate and kickstart the economy. An example of this is, find a place that sells gold low, and bring it across the world to where it is bought high.

Quests can overlap and unlock new quests from within them. For example, Epic Quests can have several medium-sized quests inside of them, some of which the players might think are independent and not even part of the larger quest. The smaller quest might also be part of several quests.

With all of the above it should seem as though there are a myriad of options for the players.

### Environmental Quests: 

These they find in the environment and not an NPC. This is a scene and the player must discover what the information around tells them to be able to start.

Everything is a task in the game. Every mob will be tracked and the player will get rewards that help their character (not just gold) Some of these can be titles. Eg, the player kills a lot of rats, they get the title Vanquisher of the Vermin. They could also get a special item or attribute.

## Dungeons

Dungeons are a type of quest and playable area, that and again is just a useful word to describe an area to be solved. The word dungeon, in-game, should be used as a jail in a castle.

Dungeons are solvable puzzles, usually with a boss or mini-boss that a group of players, or a player by themselves, can traverse to find and end result and get  treasure and skills. They are places that have secret passages, kill unique skilled NPCs, and retrieve rare artifacts. Dungeons maybe be permeable and in context with other non-dungeon areas, such as the sewer below New Pallamost but they may also follow the rules of seamless everworld, where they are whole new playable areas.   
Dungeons can also be assigned a Level in our documentation (but not in game), to describe the difficulty and the loot table to be assigned with it.   
Dungeons may be a step in a larger quest, or be stand-alone. They may be themed as part of a quest, or themed with some other metanarrative. 

# 

# 

# Epic Quests

Epic quests are very large in scope and should take several months of player time to complete. They involved major parts of the world and change the outcome of the world lore and game by the end. They should contain several other quests as part of them. These are highly competitive to complete, as only the player, or party, that completes them gets the final reward.

A new Epic Quest should be added at each major, whole number release.

# The Fisher King 

Location: All Worlds  
Pre-requisite: Azernath Kings   
The errant and ailing king of New Pallamost, find where he has gone and try to restore him to the throne and return New Pallamost to its rightful glory.

BACK STORY:

At the end of the Wars of the Third Age, the ailing king sent his only son, his heir into hiding as a baby.

Joyzil Greymayne, a once great and powerful king of a great and powerful kingdom is near death. The Wars have done their worst on his psyche, and the wounds he’s suffered are incapable of being healed. To guard against usurpers he has sent  his baby son far away, to live with peasants, where Joyzil stays and needs a constant supply of Aqua Vitae from the Kingdom of the Wood to stay alive.

Greymayne hardly holds court anymore and in his stead has named Ayrchek his minister plenipotentary to deal the many foreign matters in these dark times. This surprised most of the court as Ayrchek was a commoner from one of the conquested colonies, but grew up with Greymayne children, daughter Frandaye and the lost heir. Greymayne trusted Arychek more than any other advisor and thinks of him as his son, and where Greymayne stays locked in his castle, Ayrchek greets guests to the court and is out around town, and makes diplomatic missions to Kingdom of the Wood, gothigport and other kingdoms. His main goals are to keep a war from happening between gothigport and themselves, and to regain control of their most recent and largest colony, Ghazmelestine, far in the western wild. Pallamost has run out of resources and this is their last hope to return to greatness. Ghazmelestine, though, is cursed and now just a parched desert, but many of the techno-prophets say there are great riches under the land.  
There are a lot of threats to New Pallamost in Ghazmelestine, since they were invaders and the local villages despise them. The close advisors think that this is where the heir was sent. 

No one knows where the heir was sent except Frandeye and the heir’s attendant, Threskin, who spies on the heir from afar. Even the Heir himself does not know his destiny. Greymayne doesn’t even know if his heir is still alive.

Ghazmelestine blames the king for the curse and part of this quest is to return the heir back to the throne and remove the curse from Ghazmelestine making it again a fertile land, making the people their love the king once again.

REWARDS:  
The Player gets to marry Frandey (or Ayrchek) and be on the court to the new Heir. They become sergeant of their own legion of the Pallatian Guard, and possibly in line for the throne for themselves someday. Access to a portion of the crown jewels. A path to become King (or Queen)

## Forbidden Rising (By RogueSpartan)

In the main quest-line, the player discovers that there is a rising power called the Forbidden Truth trying to ascend their leader to become a god, through dubious sacrifices. The main quest-giver will provide the player with a pretty straightforward goal, but with multiple possibilities. 

Beginning: The Origins of War

“In the North, there is a group growing in power. They call themselves the Forbidden Truth. Apparently they want to become gods or something. I don’t really know all the details, but hey, if you want to figure it out, go ahead.”

Decision: Divided 3 ways, go to the capital of each kingdom and find an attendant of the court to give you more information on how bad the Forbidden Truth is, and how they’re trying to stop it, so you have to join them, blah blah blah.

OR: Travel north and come across one of their sacrificial temples, and get inducted as a member by killing an NPC.

Key decision: To Kill a God

This one is a bit trickier, as it has 4 different possibilities. 3 depending on your kingdom, and 1 if you’re part of the cult. 

Decision: Once more, 3 ways depending on your kingdom. It works sort of like rock paper scissors, as each kingdom has one that they are hunting, and one that they are hunted by. For example, Faith attacks Progress, Progress attacks Tradition, and Tradition attacks Faith. I’ll flesh out the reasoning for each later, especially when we write out NPC quest dialogue. The Gods that are being hunted are the Deluvic ones listed above. Depending on Kingdom alliance, you will hunt one god for a piece of their soul to return them to their realm of origin (Endaric or Aetheric) so they can no longer exist in Deluvia. I think upon reaching the god, there will be two options available to the player. One, will be simply to fight the god a PNPC that will result in the drop of the soul shard (a renamed end crystal). The other option is to do it completely in roleplay, essentially trying to convince the god to hand over their shard as the player is considered worthy. I see this going three ways depending on the boss. Progress (God of knowledge) requires a hefty Intelligence stat, Traditional (God of Leadership) requires a strong Charisma stat, and Faith (God of War) requires a strong Strength stat. 

OR: As this is a much less desirable path by players, the difficulty and yield will be much higher. Every player in this path has to defeat not one, but all three of the gods, retrieving their shards to sacrifice to the cult leader for ascension. 

Final section: Ending Ascension / Gods Among Us

This is the final result of the questline, and a turning point for the history of the game. It is actually a large server event, held for multiple weeks during probably a month or so, and it is basically a massive PVP event. After the decisions of the prior quests, the players will be tasked to defeat or defend the cult leader during his ascension ceremony. Now, here’s where it gets interesting. The Cult Leader boss (PNPC) will be given extra armor, health, and even weapons, based on how many shards were retrieved by players allied in his quest line. The fights will take place in the weeks before his ascension, as the kingdoms are trying to weaken him before he has a chance to ascend. The battles will be between 1-8 player teams from the kingdoms, versus 1-4 player teams from the cult \+ the cult leader boss. Now, the kingdom teams also have a benefit on their side. Depending on which god was killed the most, the players from every kingdom will receive a special weapon that emphasizes that god’s powers. 

Results: Should the Kingdoms succeed and weaken the boss enough to a point where he cannot ascend, they shall be victorious, and the players will get an extra reward from their kingdom of choice, along with the rewards gained if they or their party defeat the cult leader.

OR: Should the Kingdoms fail, the Cult leader shall ascend to god status, and enter the Aetheric realm. As a reward for their compliance, he gives his followers an extra reward on top of what they gained if they or their party defeated the onslaught party. 

Lore changes: This is a big one. As this concludes chapter one of the server, we will add in the results of player decisions into the lore. 

The Kingdoms- The Kingdom that had the most success (quest completion) will be deemed the most powerful of the period, and the other two shall also be labeled in kind. 

The Gods- The god that was killed the most will now be considered bound to his prior realm. He will no longer exist in Deluvia, essentially leaving a void for the Kingdom that benefitted from that god the most.

The Cult- This one hinges entirely on the results of the event. Should the Kingdoms succeed and trump the cult leader, the cult will become less influential, and the leader will eventually begin looking into other methods to ascend, leading to the decline of the cult following through the years. The more interesting scenario is if the cult succeeds and he ascends. If he manages to ascend, he will take his place as the new god of the occult, embodying all that is involved with sacrifice and blood magic. He is considered the god of contracts, and will become perhaps something for a later quest-line.

# Dungeons

Dungeons are areas overcome by mobs. They are usually one, contained location that the character has to solve physical puzzles in and defeat a bunch of mobs. They get to defeat a mini-boss about half way, and then the main boss at the end to get the rare loot.  
They should fit in the the lore.

## Tower of Wrath

**Location: Wildlands**

## Jutrollag Basilica

 (Kalimvane)  
 This is the first dungeon the players might encounter. This was the first settlement of the Jutrollag pilgrims who set up the big basilica in honor of their god Expitik. Expitik has long gone from the basilica and all that are left are monsters. 

BACKSTORY: Expitik is a good goddess and was outcast from gothigport when they turned their backs on gods and magic long ago.   
The Jutrollag Union Brotherhood was an old and respected guild at gothigport. Terriss was the lead cleric and Uftan was his cupholder. This was at a time when there were many guilds on gothigport and many had their own religions.   
gothigport started to dive deeper into technology after the Wars of the Third Age. Any type of arcane thinking was shunned and Expitik was the first to go, as she was most nature-based diety on the islands. Once her holy tree was cut down she fled and her followers were massacred by a techno-cult mob. Expitik and the escaping Jutrollags came to Kalimvane and founded and built the basilica in her honor for delivering them through the deluge and Dreadstorms.   
Terris was their loyal leader and powerful in Expitik miracola (miracles). Uftan was his protoge but wanted the miracola faster than Terris would allow. Becoming impatient, Uftan went back to gothigport, which in the short 11 years, had become a crawling techo-conurbanation, seeking forgiveness and acceptance. He met secretly with House Grimstok which he made a bargain to become a lackey in the House if he gave up his religion and miracola. He did, for 2 years but longed for Kalimvane, the Jutrollag’s and Expitik. He voyaged back to Kalimvane and stole the automaton Thegot from the Grimstok factory. When he reached Kalimvane, Terris was dead, murdered by the native barbarians of Kwinst. Uftan was so overcome with pain that he and Thegot, who he had to reprogram, went on a revenge murder spree of the Kwinst. For this Expitik had no pity and banished Uftan from the basilica. Some of the Jutrollags followed Uftan to build the town at the current location it is now. Expitik left the basilica with the rest of the followers to an unknown location. She cursed the basilica and the area to be overrun with monsters. Uftan and the rest of the citizens built walls and a moat around the city to help keep the monsters at bay.   
Now Uftan prefers this history to be hidden and never spoken of. Only the original members of the Jutrollags, which there are 3 others, know the story. Everyone else in Kalimvane are newcomers. He has made Kalimvane into the trading center of that region of the Eastern Rim though, because of the monsters, commerce is suffering.   
He wants to make sure that House Grimstok can’t find him. He has a lot of worries on his mind.

The other three members from the Jutrollags are Vanfang, who went off to found the thieves guild; Bildagar, who is now a hermit in the Boarsback; and Gregari, a merchant in the town. By finding and talking to all three of these, and completing the Jutrollag Basilica dungeon, will open up the quest to discover this mystery.

For now, all the player knows is this is a simple trading town. And all they know is that the basilica is a monster haven

# Events

Events time specific and location specific. We try to make them not as expected Minecraft events, but wrapped in roleplay, and tied into the lore of the world.

## Festival of Dolstide (New Pallamost) 

\- A festival for the King’s birthday, a grand warrior tournament. Each kingdom sends their best warrior for the revels

## The Horogradrome (Gothigport) \- 

* Stelmsreev \- a game of skill and agility  
* Mecho-derby battles, many of the guilds and gang unions have an official league of sport. Last mech standing wins.

## Skiff runner racing 

(gothigport) \- Illegal, underground modded skiff runner racing in the canals of gothigport. 

## Enchantment of the Ring

# Class Quests: 

# Wanderer: Seeking the Twelve

Twelve quests, each one embodying the aspects of the Twelve Elder Sages of Deluvia, who were the first to arrive in Deluvia after the Age of Gods.  
The player can start in any order, though some are harder than others, and by the end, they must choose one Elder Sage to bind to and complete a thirteenth quest which gives them.

Any classes can choose one of the Elder Sages to seek, but the Wanderer gets to seek all twelve.

The Twelve Elder Sages hold the physical world together with their combined virtues. They imbue their virtues into objects in the physical world that can manifest themselves into abilities and knowledge.  
Travelers in Deluvia can obtain knowledge of the virtues of the Elder Sages by making a pilgrimage to one of the Elder Sages. Each pilgrimage is fraught with danger as each Sage secludes themselves and purposely makes themselves difficult to locate to test the will and worthiness of each pilgrim.  
The Twelve Sages were the creators gods gift to the races as the end of the Second Age dwindled to provide their virtues from themselves onto the next progeny. Only the three original creator gods participated in which is why it is a direct line to them, and other virtues exist from the whole pantheon that are not listed here.  
The Twelve Sage:  
The First: The first to come into the Third Age. The conceiver of Knowledge.  
The Aggressor: The first to strike and see opportunity. The wielder of physical power and cunning to gain territory for their fellow clan.  
The Cleric: Seeks balance through transformation and commune with gods.  
The Leader: Holds power to sway their fellowkind to greatness in battle and to govern.  
The Judge: Finds fairness through discernment  
The Free Spirit: Not beholden to any other law. Finds strength in serendipity.  
The Warrior: Has skill in battle and tactics.  
The Prosperous One: Has much land and coin.  
The Scholar: The holder of knowledge from books.  
The Merchant: The crafter and seller of goods. Makes good deals.  
The Transformer: Transmuter of physical substances  
The Consumer: Hungry for information and resources and the spark of existence.

Find these Sages throughout Deluvia and seek the wisdom they have to survive in this world.

# Ranger: Mystery of the Wood

A portion of the Kingdom of the Wood Cycle of quests. This gives the Ranger an edge in solving the main questline.  
All classes can do the Wood Cycle, this quests just gives the Ranger a jump start about the mystery.

# Mage: The Awakening

Twelve Circles of magic that the Mage can find a master archmage to train them in one of the circles, opening up many new spells. 

This is the path (of

# Cleric: Plight of the Damned

The cleric makes a pilgrimage to New Pallamost for the Fellowship of Dolstide to participate as an acolyte in the Oath of the Paladin in the Pallas Cathedral. Here they find out some new pilgrimages they are able to partake in as well as The ShadowTide, whether to stop it, or be turned to join it.

# Rogue: Cartel of Thieves

The Rogue learns of the underground economy in gothigport and wishes to be part of it. The new found guild is set on disrupting the gothigport ruler’s grip on the economy and making some profit on the way.

## Fighter: Might Makes Right

The fighter gets to train to fight in the Horogradrome with either the Stelmsreev or Mechi-derby battles. The winner gets an at-large entry into the Revels of Dolstide Grand Tournament of Deluvia in New Pallamost (something only Kingdoms can usually enter)
